  apiKey: process.env.FIREMOON_API_KEY,
});

const result = await generateImage({
  model: firemoon.image('flux/dev'),
  prompt: 'A beautiful landscape with an orangered moon in the background',

### Enable Web Search for GPT-5 with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

This example illustrates how to integrate real-time web search capabilities into GPT-5 using the AI SDK. By configuring the `web_search` tool with `searchContextSize`, the model can access up-to-date information and the snippet also shows how to retrieve the URL sources from the result.

```ts
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in AI this week?',
  tools: {
    web_search: openai.tools.webSearch({
      searchContextSize: 'high',
    }),
  },
});

// Access URL sources
const sources = result.sources;
```

### Migrate AI SDK Model Instance from Completions to Responses API (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

This example illustrates the migration process from the OpenAI Completions API to the Responses API by changing how the model instance is created. It shows the 'before' (Completions API) and 'after' (Responses API) syntax for `generateText` calls.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Completions API
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Explain the concept of quantum entanglement.',
});

// Responses API
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Explain the concept of quantum entanglement.',
});
```

### Create POST Route Handler with streamText in TanStack Start

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

Creates a server-side POST route handler that accepts chat messages, converts them from UIMessage format to ModelMessage format, calls streamText to generate a response, and returns a streamed UI response. The handler uses TanStack Start's createFileRoute and server handlers pattern.

```typescript
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/api/chat')({
  server: {
    handlers: {
      POST: async ({ request }) => {
        const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

        const result = streamText({
          model: __MODEL__,
          messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
        });

        return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
      },
    },
  },
});
```

### Configure Vercel AI Gateway Provider

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

Demonstrates three equivalent ways to configure the Vercel AI Gateway as the model provider: using the default global provider with a string reference, importing gateway from the 'ai' package, or importing from the '@ai-sdk/gateway' package. All methods support model selection via string identifiers.

```typescript
// Option 1: Default global provider (string reference)
model: __MODEL__;
```

```typescript
// Option 2: Import from 'ai' package (included by default)
import { gateway } from 'ai';
model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5');
```

```typescript
// Option 3: Install and import from '@ai-sdk/gateway' package
import { gateway } from '@ai-sdk/gateway';
model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5');
```

### Control o3-mini Reasoning Effort with AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o3

Example showing how to adjust the reasoning effort level for o3-mini using the reasoningEffort parameter. This parameter accepts 'low', 'medium', or 'high' values to control the amount of computation the model expends on internal reasoning before generating a response.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Reduce reasoning effort for faster responses
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement briefly.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: { reasoningEffort: 'low' },
  },
});
```

### Add Temperature Conversion Tool to AI SDK Route Handler (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

This example extends the AI SDK route handler by adding a new `convertFahrenheitToCelsius` tool. This tool is defined within the `tools` object of the `streamText` configuration, providing a description, an `inputSchema` for temperature conversion, and an `execute` function to perform the calculation. It allows the model to convert Fahrenheit temperatures to Celsius as part of its multi-step process.

```tsx
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/api/chat')({
  server: {
    handlers: {
      POST: async ({ request }) => {
        const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

        const result = streamText({
          model: __MODEL__,
          messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
          stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
          tools: {
            weather: tool({
              description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
              inputSchema: z.object({
                location: z
                  .string()
                  .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
              }),
              execute: async ({ location }) => {
                const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
                return {
                  location,
                  temperature,
                };
              },
            }),
            convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
              description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
              inputSchema: z.object({
                temperature: z
                  .number()
                  .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
              }),
              execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
                const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
                return {
                  celsius,
                };
              },
            }),
          },
        });

        return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
      },
    },
  },
});
```

### Use Google Search Grounding with Gemini

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gemini

Integrate Google Search with Gemini 3 to access real-time information and provide grounded responses. This example shows how to use the googleSearch tool and access grounding metadata and safety ratings from the response.

```typescript
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-3-pro-preview'),
  tools: {
    google_search: google.tools.googleSearch({}),
  },
  prompt:
    'List the top 5 San Francisco news from the past week.' +
    'You must include the date of each article.',
});

// access the grounding metadata. Casting to the provider metadata type
// is optional but provides autocomplete and type safety.
const metadata = providerMetadata?.google as
  | GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata
  | undefined;
const groundingMetadata = metadata?.groundingMetadata;
const safetyRatings = metadata?.safetyRatings;

console.log({ text, sources, groundingMetadata, safetyRatings });
```

--------------------------------

### Implement Tool Calling for Multi-Step Workflows

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gemini

Use Gemini 3's tool calling capabilities to enable multi-step workflows with improved reliability. This example demonstrates defining a weather tool and using stepCountIs to control the number of tool invocations.

```typescript
import { z } from 'zod';
import { generateText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';

const result = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-3-pro-preview'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5), // enables multi-step calling
});

console.log(result.text);

console.log(result.steps);
```

### Integrate DeepSeek R1 via Groq with Reasoning Extraction

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/r1

This TypeScript example demonstrates connecting to Groq's `deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b` model using the AI SDK. Similar to other third-party integrations, it employs `wrapLanguageModel` and `extractReasoningMiddleware` to capture and return the model's reasoning process, identified by a 'think' tag, along with the generated text.

```ts
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import {
  generateText,
  wrapLanguageModel,
  extractReasoningMiddleware,
} from 'ai';

// middleware to extract reasoning tokens
const enhancedModel = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: groq('deepseek-r1-distill-llama-70b'),
  middleware: extractReasoningMiddleware({ tagName: 'think' }),
});

const { reasoningText, text } = await generateText({
  model: enhancedModel,
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement.',
});
```

  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'Analyze this complex dataset and provide insights.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      reasoningEffort: 'high', // Increases autonomous exploration
    },

### Define and Use Custom Tools with GPT-5 via AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

This example illustrates how to implement custom tool calling with GPT-5 using the AI SDK. It shows how to define a `getWeather` tool with a `zod` schema for input validation and an asynchronous `execute` function, allowing the model to interact with external systems for specific tasks.

```ts
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { toolResults } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Generate Reference-to-Video with Alibaba AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/alibaba

This example illustrates how to generate a video using reference images or videos for character consistency with the Alibaba AI SDK. It employs `alibaba.video('wan2.6-r2v-flash')` and includes `referenceUrls` in `providerOptions.alibaba` to guide character generation. Character identifiers can be used in the prompt to link to the references.

```ts
import { alibaba, type AlibabaVideoModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/alibaba';
import { experimental_generateVideo as generateVideo } from 'ai';

const { video } = await generateVideo({
  model: alibaba.video('wan2.6-r2v-flash'),
  prompt: 'character1 walks through a beautiful garden and waves at the camera',
  resolution: '1280x720',
  duration: 5,
  providerOptions: {
    alibaba: {
      referenceUrls: ['https://example.com/character-reference.jpg'],
      pollTimeoutMs: 600000
    } satisfies AlibabaVideoModelOptions
  }
});
```

  },

### Configure Web Search Tool with Query Metadata in AI SDK Responses API (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

This example illustrates how to provide query-specific metadata to the `webSearchPreview` tool to improve search result quality. It includes options like `searchContextSize` and `userLocation` to refine the search context.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o-mini'),
  prompt: 'What happened in San Francisco last week?',
  tools: {
    web_search_preview: openai.tools.webSearchPreview({
      searchContextSize: 'high',
      userLocation: {
        type: 'approximate',
        city: 'San Francisco',
        region: 'California',
      },
    }),
  },
});

console.log(result.text);
console.log(result.sources);
```

### Create Server Action with streamUI and Tool Integration

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

Demonstrates how to create a Server Action using AI SDK's streamUI function with DeepInfra's Llama model. The example shows tool definition with Zod schema validation and generator function that yields loading state before returning final weather component. This enables dynamic UI streaming based on AI model decisions.

```typescript
'use server';

import { streamUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function streamComponent() {
  const result = await streamUI({
    model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
    prompt: 'Get the weather for San Francisco',
    text: ({ content }) => <div>{content}</div>,
    tools: {
      getWeather: {
        description: 'Get the weather for a location',
        inputSchema: z.object({ location: z.string() }),
        generate: async function* ({ location }) {
          yield <div>loading...</div>;
          const weather = '25c'; // await getWeather(location);
          return (
            <div>
              the weather in {location} is {weather}.
            </div>
          );
        },
      },
    },
  });
  return result.value;
}
```

### Configure Multi-Step Tool Calls in AI SDK Route Handler (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

This snippet demonstrates how to modify an AI SDK route handler to enable multi-step tool calls. By setting `stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)` within the `streamText` function, the model is allowed to perform up to 5 steps, including executing tools and generating responses, before stopping. It takes user messages as input and streams back UI messages.

```tsx
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/api/chat')({
  server: {
    handlers: {
      POST: async ({ request }) => {
        const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

        const result = streamText({
          model: __MODEL__,
          messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
          stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
          tools: {
            weather: tool({
              description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
              inputSchema: z.object({
                location: z
                  .string()
                  .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
              }),
              execute: async ({ location }) => {
                const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
                return {
                  location,
                  temperature,
                };
              },
            }),
          },
        });

        return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
      },
    },
  },
});
```

--------------------------------

### Using addToolInputExamplesMiddleware with AI SDK for Text Generation

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/add-tool-input-examples-middleware

This example demonstrates how to integrate `addToolInputExamplesMiddleware` into an AI SDK application. It shows wrapping a language model with the middleware to enhance a `weather` tool's description with formatted input examples before generating text based on a prompt.

```ts
import {
  generateText,
  tool,
  wrapLanguageModel,
  addToolInputExamplesMiddleware,
} from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const model = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: __MODEL__,
  middleware: addToolInputExamplesMiddleware({
    prefix: 'Input Examples:',
    format: (example, index) =>
      `${index + 1}. ${JSON.stringify(example.input)}`,
  }),
});

const result = await generateText({
  model,
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({ location: z.string() }),
      inputExamples: [
        { input: { location: 'San Francisco' } },
        { input: { location: 'London' } },
      ],
    }),
  },
  prompt: 'What is the weather in Tokyo?',
});
```

### Enable Extended Thinking with Interleaved Tool Use in Claude 4

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/claude-4

Advanced example showing how to enable extended thinking capabilities in Claude 4 with a specified token budget and interleaved thinking beta feature. This allows Claude to perform step-by-step reasoning and alternate between thinking and tool use for complex problem-solving.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoningText, reasoning } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-20250514'),
  prompt: 'How will quantum computing impact cryptography by 2050?',
  providerOptions: {
    anthropic: {
      thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 15000 },
    } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
  },
  headers: {
    'anthropic-beta': 'interleaved-thinking-2025-05-14',
  },
});

console.log(text); // text response
console.log(reasoningText); // reasoning text
console.log(reasoning); // reasoning details including redacted reasoning
```

### Implement Chat UI with AI SDK `useChat` Hook in React/TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

This TypeScript React component (`src/routes/index.tsx`) sets up a basic chat interface. It utilizes the `@ai-sdk/react` `useChat` hook to manage chat messages and send user input to an LLM API, and `useState` for local input management. The component renders a list of messages and an input field for user interaction.

```tsx
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/')({
  component: Chat,
});

function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Create Chat UI Component with Vue and AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nuxt

Sets up a Vue component that initializes a Chat instance from @ai-sdk/vue, manages user input with ref, and renders chat messages with role-based formatting. The component handles form submission to send messages and displays AI responses through the message parts array. Requires @ai-sdk/vue package and Vue 3 with script setup syntax.

```typescript
<script setup lang="ts">
import { Chat } from "@ai-sdk/vue";
import { ref } from "vue";

const input = ref("");
const chat = new Chat({});

const handleSubmit = (e: Event) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input.value });
    input.value = "";
};
</script>

<template>
    <div>
        <div v-for="(m, index) in chat.messages" :key="m.id ? m.id : index">
            {{ m.role === "user" ? "User: " : "AI: " }}
            <div
                v-for="(part, index) in m.parts"
                :key="`${m.id}-${part.type}-${index}`"
            >
                <div v-if="part.type === 'text'">{{ part.text }}</div>
            </div>
        </div>

        <form @submit="handleSubmit">
            <input v-model="input" placeholder="Say something..." />
        </form>
    </div>
</template>
```

### Control GPT-5 Response Verbosity with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

This snippet demonstrates how to adjust the response length of GPT-5 using the AI SDK's `textVerbosity` option. It shows examples for both 'low' (concise) and 'high' (detailed) verbosity settings without modifying the original prompt, providing flexibility in response generation.

```ts
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Concise response
const { text: conciseText } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'Explain quantum computing.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      textVerbosity: 'low', // Produces terse, minimal responses
    },
  },
});

// Detailed response
const { text: detailedText } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'Explain quantum computing.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      textVerbosity: 'high', // Produces comprehensive, detailed responses
    },
  },
});
```

### Persist Chat History using previousResponseId in AI SDK Responses API (TypeScript/TSX)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

This example shows how to persist chat history across multiple `generateText` calls by passing the `responseId` of a previous model response. This allows the model to access the full conversation context for subsequent messages.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result1 = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o-mini'),
  prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
});

const result2 = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o-mini'),
  prompt: 'Summarize in 2 sentences',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      previousResponseId: result1.providerMetadata?.openai.responseId as string,
    },
  },
});
```

### Generate Structured JSON Object with AI SDK Core (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o3

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to use `generateObject` from AI SDK Core with an OpenAI model and a Zod schema to produce type-safe, structured JSON output. It's ideal for tasks requiring specific data formats, such as extracting information or generating synthetic data based on a defined structure.

```ts
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});
```

### Generate Structured JSON Data with Zod Schema

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

import { generateObject } from 'ai';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o'),

      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),

### Handle Assistant Thread Started Events in Slack with TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/slackbot

Processes Slack assistant thread started events by posting a welcome message and setting up suggested prompts to guide user interactions. Uses the Slack Web API client to manage thread initialization and prompt configuration. Requires proper channel and thread identifiers from the event payload.

```typescript
import type { AssistantThreadStartedEvent } from '@slack/web-api';
import { client } from './slack-utils';

export async function assistantThreadMessage(
  event: AssistantThreadStartedEvent,
) {
  const { channel_id, thread_ts } = event.assistant_thread;
  console.log(`Thread started: ${channel_id} ${thread_ts}`);
  console.log(JSON.stringify(event));

  await client.chat.postMessage({
    channel: channel_id,
    thread_ts: thread_ts,
    text: "Hello, I'm an AI assistant built with the AI SDK by Vercel!",
  });

  await client.assistant.threads.setSuggestedPrompts({
    channel_id: channel_id,
    thread_ts: thread_ts,
    prompts: [
      {
        title: 'Get the weather',
        message: 'What is the current weather in London?',
      },
      {
        title: 'Get the news',
        message: 'What is the latest Premier League news from the BBC?',
      },
    ],
  });
}
```

This example illustrates how to generate a video using an image as a starting frame combined with an optional text prompt. It uses the `grok-imagine-video` model, specifying the input image via a URL and a text description for the video's content, along with `duration` and `pollTimeoutMs`.

import { xai, type XaiVideoModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { experimental_generateVideo as generateVideo } from 'ai';

const { videos } = await generateVideo({

### Implement AI SDK Example Provider Factory Function in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/openai-compatible-providers/custom-providers

This TypeScript function `createExample` initializes and returns an AI SDK provider instance. It handles base URL configuration, API key loading, and header generation. The function then creates and exposes methods for instantiating various OpenAI-compatible models (chat, completion, embedding, image) with common configuration, making it a central factory for AI model access.

```ts
export function createExample(
  options: ExampleProviderSettings = {},
): ExampleProvider {
  const baseURL = withoutTrailingSlash(
    options.baseURL ?? 'https://api.example.com/v1',
  );
  const getHeaders = () => ({
    Authorization: `Bearer ${loadApiKey({
      apiKey: options.apiKey,
      environmentVariableName: 'EXAMPLE_API_KEY',
      description: 'Example API key',
    })}`,
    ...options.headers,
  });

  interface CommonModelConfig {
    provider: string;
    url: ({ path }: { path: string }) => string;
    headers: () => Record<string, string>;
    fetch?: FetchFunction;
  }

  const getCommonModelConfig = (modelType: string): CommonModelConfig => ({
    provider: `example.${modelType}`,
    url: ({ path }) => {
      const url = new URL(`${baseURL}${path}`);
      if (options.queryParams) {
        url.search = new URLSearchParams(options.queryParams).toString();
      }
      return url.toString();
    },
    headers: getHeaders,
    fetch: options.fetch,
  });

  const createChatModel = (
    modelId: ExampleChatModelId,
    settings: ExampleChatSettings = {},
  ) => {
    return new OpenAICompatibleChatLanguageModel(
      modelId,
      settings,
      getCommonModelConfig('chat'),
    );
  };

  const createCompletionModel = (
    modelId: ExampleCompletionModelId,
    settings: ExampleCompletionSettings = {},
  ) =>
    new OpenAICompatibleCompletionLanguageModel(
      modelId,
      settings,
      getCommonModelConfig('completion'),
    );

  const createEmbeddingModel = (
    modelId: ExampleEmbeddingModelId,
    settings: ExampleEmbeddingSettings = {},
  )
    =>
    new OpenAICompatibleEmbeddingModel(
      modelId,
      settings,
      getCommonModelConfig('embedding'),
    );

  const createImageModel = (
    modelId: ExampleImageModelId,
    settings: ExampleImageSettings = {},
  )
    =>
    new OpenAICompatibleImageModel(
      modelId,
      settings,
      getCommonModelConfig('image'),
    );

  const provider = (
    modelId: ExampleChatModelId,
    settings?: ExampleChatSettings,
  ) => createChatModel(modelId, settings);

  provider.completionModel = createCompletionModel;
  provider.chatModel = createChatModel;
  provider.embeddingModel = createEmbeddingModel;
  provider.imageModel = createImageModel;

  return provider;
}

// Export default instance
export const example = createExample();
```

### Display AI SDK Tool Calls in React UI Component

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

This snippet updates the client-side React UI component (`src/routes/index.tsx`) to correctly display different types of message parts received from the AI SDK. It iterates through `message.parts` and uses a `switch` statement to render 'text' parts normally and 'tool-weather' parts as a JSON string for debugging or detailed display.

```tsx
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/')({
  component: Chat,
});

function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
              case 'tool-weather':
                return (
                  <pre key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>
                    {JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}
                  </pre>
                );
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Integrate Custom Tools with AI SDK for External Interactions (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

This example illustrates how to define and use custom tools with the AI SDK's 'generateText' function. It shows how to pass a 'tool' object with a description, input schema (using Zod), and an 'execute' function to extend the LLM's capabilities. The 'getWeather' tool simulates fetching weather data for a given location, allowing the model to interact with external logic.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Define Weather Tool in AI SDK Route Handler (TypeScript/React)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

This snippet modifies the server-side route handler (`src/routes/api/chat.ts`) to integrate a new 'weather' tool. It uses `streamText` from 'ai' to process messages, `tool` to define the weather functionality, and `zod` for input schema validation. The `execute` function simulates fetching weather data based on a provided location.

```tsx
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages, tool } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { z } from 'zod';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/api/chat')({
  server: {
    handlers: {
      POST: async ({ request }) => {
        const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();

        const result = streamText({
          model: __MODEL__,
          messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
          tools: {
            weather: tool({
              description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
              inputSchema: z.object({
                location: z
                  .string()
                  .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
              }),
              execute: async ({ location }) => {
                const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
                return {
                  location,
                  temperature,
                };
              },
            }),
          },
        });

        return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
      },
    },
  },
});
```

### Build Streaming Chat Agent with TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

Create an interactive chat application using the AI SDK's streamText function. The agent maintains conversation history, streams responses in real-time to the terminal, and uses readline for user input. Requires model provider configuration via __MODEL__ and __PROVIDER_IMPORT__ placeholders.

```typescript
import { ModelMessage, streamText } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import 'dotenv/config';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: __MODEL__,
      messages,
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Generate structured JSON data with AI SDK `generateObject` and Zod schema

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o1

This example illustrates how to generate type-safe structured JSON data using the `generateObject` function with a Zod schema. It constrains the model's output to a predefined structure, making it ideal for tasks like data extraction, classification, or synthetic data generation. This functionality is supported with the 'o1' model.

```ts
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: openai('o1'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});
```

### Integrate Weather and Temperature Conversion Tools into AI SDK Agent (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

This TypeScript code snippet updates an `index.ts` file to include two distinct tools within an AI SDK agent: a `weather` tool to fetch location-based weather (returning Fahrenheit) and a `convertFahrenheitToCelsius` tool to convert temperatures. It demonstrates how to define tool schemas using `zod` and implement their `execute` logic, allowing the agent to perform multi-step reasoning and provide more accurate responses by chaining tool calls.

```typescript
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: __MODEL__,
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
        convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
          description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            temperature: z
              .number()
              .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
            const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
            return {
              celsius,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Stream GPT-5 Reasoning Summaries with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

This snippet demonstrates how to enable and stream reasoning summaries from GPT-5 using the AI SDK, providing transparency into the model's thought process. It shows how to set `reasoningSummary` in `providerOptions` and then iterate through the `fullStream` to process both `reasoning` and `text-delta` parts separately.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt:
    'Solve this logic puzzle: If all roses are flowers and some flowers fade quickly, do all roses fade quickly?',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      reasoningSummary: 'detailed', // 'auto' for condensed or 'detailed' for comprehensive
    },
  },
});

// Stream reasoning and text separately
for await (const part of result.fullStream) {
  if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
    console.log(part.textDelta);
  } else if (part.type === 'text-delta') {
    process.stdout.write(part.textDelta);
  }
}
```

### Add Weather Tool to AI Agent with streamText

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

Demonstrates how to define and integrate a weather tool into an AI agent using the AI SDK's streamText function.       model: __MODEL__,

          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,

### Add Temperature Conversion Tool to Multi-Step Pipeline in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Extends the multi-step tool configuration by adding a convertFahrenheitToCelsius tool alongside the existing weather tool. Both tools work together in the same streamText pipeline with stopWhen set to stepCountIs(5), enabling the model to fetch weather data and convert temperatures across multiple generation steps.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
      convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
        description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          temperature: z
            .number()
            .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
          const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
          return {
            celsius,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Generate Structured JSON Data with AI SDK Core and Zod (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

This snippet demonstrates how to generate type-safe JSON objects using the 'generateObject' function from AI SDK Core. It utilizes a Zod schema to define the desired output structure, ensuring the model's response conforms to a predefined format. The example generates a recipe object with nested fields like name, ingredients, and steps.

```typescript
import { generateObject } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { object } = await generateObject({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  schema: z.object({
    recipe: z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      ingredients: z.array(z.object({ name: z.string(), amount: z.string() })),
      steps: z.array(z.string()),
    }),
  }),
  prompt: 'Generate a lasagna recipe.',
});
```

### Define Tool with Input Examples for Middleware Processing

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/middleware

Demonstrates how to define a tool with `inputExamples` that will be processed by the `addToolInputExamplesMiddleware`. The middleware automatically appends the examples to the tool description in JSON format.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateText({
  model, // wrapped model from above
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string(),
      }),
      inputExamples: [
        { input: { location: 'San Francisco' } },
        { input: { location: 'London' } },
      ],
    }),
  },
  prompt: 'What is the weather in Tokyo?',
});
```

### Configure Tool Input Examples Middleware with Custom Options

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/middleware

Shows advanced configuration of `addToolInputExamplesMiddleware` with custom prefix, format function, and removal options. The format function allows customization of how examples are serialized in the tool description.

```typescript
const model = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: yourModel,
  middleware: addToolInputExamplesMiddleware({
    prefix: 'Input Examples:',
    format: (example, index) =>
      `${index + 1}. ${JSON.stringify(example.input)}`,
    remove: true,
  }),
});
```

### Configure Tool Selection by Step in ToolLoopAgent

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/loop-control

Demonstrates how to control which tools are available at different execution steps using the prepareStep callback. The example shows a three-phase workflow: search phase (steps 0-2), analysis phase (steps 3-5), and summary phase (step 6+). Each phase has different active tools and tool choice requirements.

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  tools: {
    search: searchTool,
    analyze: analyzeTool,
    summarize: summarizeTool,
  },
  prepareStep: async ({ stepNumber, steps }) => {
    // Search phase (steps 0-2)
    if (stepNumber <= 2) {
      return {
        activeTools: ['search'],
        toolChoice: 'required',
      };
    }

    // Analysis phase (steps 3-5)
    if (stepNumber <= 5) {
      return {
        activeTools: ['analyze'],
      };
    }

    // Summary phase (step 6+)
    return {
      activeTools: ['summarize'],
      toolChoice: 'required',
    };
  },
});

const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: '...',
});
```

### Initialize ToolLoopAgent with Model and Tools

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/tool-loop-agent

Creates a new ToolLoopAgent instance with a specified model, system instructions, and a collection of available tools. The agent can then be used to generate responses and execute tool calls iteratively. This example demonstrates basic setup with weather and calculator tools.

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  instructions: 'You are a helpful assistant.',
  tools: {
    weather: weatherTool,
    calculator: calculatorTool,
  },
});

const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: 'What is the weather in NYC?',
});

console.log(result.text);
```

### Transforming Existing Images with Runpod and Text Prompts (Base64) in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/runpod

This example demonstrates modifying an existing image by providing its base64 encoded string directly within the `providerOptions`. A text prompt is used to guide the image transformation, enabling in-place editing or style changes without needing to host the image externally.

```ts
// Example: Using base64 encoded image
const { image } = await generateImage({
  model: runpod.imageModel('black-forest-labs/flux-1-kontext-dev'),
  prompt: 'Make this image look like a painting',
  providerOptions: {
    runpod: {
      image: 'data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAA...', // Truncated for brevity
    },
  },
});
```

### Access Tool Calls and Results from streamText Response

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

Shows how to access and log tool calls and tool results from the streamText response object. This is useful for debugging and understanding when the agent generates tool calls instead of text responses, allowing you to display tool execution information in your chat interface.

```typescript
let fullResponse = '';
process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
  fullResponse += delta;
  process.stdout.write(delta);
}
process.stdout.write('\n\n');

console.log(await result.toolCalls);
console.log(await result.toolResults);
messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
```

### Implement Tool Calling with AI SDK Core and OpenAI (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o3

This TypeScript snippet illustrates how to integrate tool calling into an AI application using `generateText` from AI SDK Core. It defines a `getWeather` tool with an input schema, enabling the OpenAI model to invoke external functions for dynamic data retrieval, enhancing its interactive capabilities.

```ts
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o3-mini'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Configure AI Gateway Model Provider

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nuxt

Demonstrates three equivalent ways to configure the Vercel AI Gateway provider in the AI SDK: using the default global provider with a model string, importing from the 'ai' package, or importing from the '@ai-sdk/gateway' package. All methods enable access to models like Anthropic Claude.

```typescript
model: __MODEL__;
```

```typescript
// Option 1: Import from 'ai' package (included by default)
import { gateway } from 'ai';
model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5');

// Option 2: Install and import from '@ai-sdk/gateway' package
import { gateway } from '@ai-sdk/gateway';
model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5');
```

### Migrate AI SDK Provider Options from Completions to Responses API (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

This snippet demonstrates how to adapt provider-specific options when migrating from the Completions API to the Responses API. It highlights that options previously on the model provider instance are now nested within the `providerOptions` object.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Completions API
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Explain the concept of quantum entanglement.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      parallelToolCalls: false,
    },
  },
});

// Responses API
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'Explain the concept of quantum entanglement.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: {
      parallelToolCalls: false,
    },
  },
});
```

### Transcribe Audio with Gladia and Provider Options in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/gladia

This example shows how to perform an audio transcription using the `experimental_transcribe` function with a Gladia model. It includes reading an audio file and passing provider-specific options, such as enabling summarization, to customize the transcription process. This highlights how to leverage advanced Gladia features through the `providerOptions` argument.

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { gladia } from '@ai-sdk/gladia';
import { type GladiaTranscriptionModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/gladia';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: gladia.transcription(),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: {
    gladia: {
      summarization: true,
    } satisfies GladiaTranscriptionModelOptions,
  },
});
```

### Use Tako Search with AI SDK and OpenAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/tools-registry/tako-search

Implement Tako Search as a tool within the AI SDK's generateText function using OpenAI's GPT model. This example demonstrates querying stock price information with a 5-step limit and logging the generated response.

```javascript
import { takoSearch } from '@takoviz/ai-sdk';
import { generateText, stepCountIs } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-5.2',
  prompt: 'What is the stock price of Nvidia?',
  tools: {
    takoSearch: takoSearch()
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)
});

console.log(text);
```

### Generate Text with NVIDIA NIM and AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/openai-compatible-providers/nim

This example illustrates how to use the `generateText` function from the AI SDK with an NVIDIA NIM chat model to produce text based on a given prompt. It demonstrates the full flow from provider setup to logging the generated text, token usage, and the finish reason of the generation.

```typescript
import { createOpenAICompatible } from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const nim = createOpenAICompatible({
  name: 'nim',
  baseURL: 'https://integrate.api.nvidia.com/v1',
  headers: {
    Authorization: `Bearer ${process.env.NIM_API_KEY}`,
  },
});

const { text, usage, finishReason } = await generateText({
  model: nim.chatModel('deepseek-ai/deepseek-r1'),
  prompt: 'Tell me the history of the San Francisco Mission-style burrito.',
});

console.log(text);
console.log('Token usage:', usage);
console.log('Finish reason:', finishReason);
```

### React Chat Component with Tool Rendering - TypeScript/TSX

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/tanstack-start

A TanStack Router-based React component that renders a chat interface with support for multiple tool types including weather and temperature conversion. The component manages message state, handles user input submission, and displays tool outputs as formatted JSON. It uses the @ai-sdk/react useChat hook to manage conversation state and message sending.

```typescript
import { createFileRoute } from '@tanstack/react-router';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export const Route = createFileRoute('/')({ 
  component: Chat,
});

function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
              case 'tool-weather':
              case 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius':
                return (
                  <pre key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>
                    {JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}
                  </pre>
                );
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Implement Custom Download Function for AI SDK Models

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/prompts

This example shows how to provide a custom `experimental_download` function to `generateText` for advanced control over file downloading. It allows implementing custom logic for throttling, retries, authentication, or caching for files referenced by URLs, especially for models that don't natively support URL-based file inputs. Note that this feature is experimental and subject to change.

```javascript
const result = await generateText({
  model: "anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5",
  experimental_download: async (
    requestedDownloads: Array<{
      url: URL;
      isUrlSupportedByModel: boolean;
    }>,
  ): PromiseLike<
    Array<{
      data: Uint8Array;
      mediaType: string | undefined;
    } | null>
  > => {
    // ... download the files and return an array with similar order
  },
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'file',
          data: new URL('https://api.company.com/private/document.pdf'),
          mediaType: 'application/pdf',
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Create Chat Route Handler with Next.js and OpenAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

Set up a POST route handler for the chat endpoint that streams text responses from OpenAI's GPT-5 model. The handler accepts messages, converts them to model format, and returns a UI message stream response with a 30-second timeout.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-5'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

--------------------------------

### Implement useChat Hook for Real-time Chat Interface

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/deepseek-v3-2

Build a React client component using the useChat hook to handle real-time messaging. The component manages input state, displays messages with role identification, and handles form submission to send messages to the AI endpoint.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            if (part.type === 'text' || part.type === 'reasoning') {
              return <div key={index}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
            return null;
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

--------------------------------

### Dynamic Model Selection with prepareStep Callback

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/loop-control

Demonstrates how to use the prepareStep callback to dynamically switch models based on execution context. This example upgrades to a stronger model after initial steps when the conversation becomes more complex.

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: 'openai/gpt-4o-mini', // Default model
  tools: {
    // your tools
  },
  prepareStep: async ({ stepNumber, messages }) => {
    // Use a stronger model for complex reasoning after initial steps
    if (stepNumber > 2 && messages.length > 10) {
      return {
        model: __MODEL__,
      };
    }
    // Continue with default settings
    return {};
  },
});

const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: '...',
});
```

### Build Chat Interface with useChat Hook in Next.js

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o1

Implements a client-side chat component using the useChat hook from AI SDK React. Displays message history with role identification and provides a form for user input that automatically communicates with the backend API endpoint.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

export default function Page() {
  const { messages, input, handleInputChange, handleSubmit, error } = useChat();

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.content}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input name="prompt" value={input} onChange={handleInputChange} />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Initialize AI SDK MCP Clients, Retrieve Tools, and Generate Text in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/node/mcp-tools

Illustrates the complete workflow for using MCP tools with the AI SDK. It shows how to create clients for stdio, HTTP, and SSE MCP servers, fetch tools from each, combine them, and then pass them to `generateText` for AI model interaction. The example includes necessary imports, error handling, and ensures all client resources are properly closed.

```typescript
import { createMCPClient } from '@ai-sdk/mcp';
import { generateText, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { Experimental_StdioMCPTransport } from '@ai-sdk/mcp/mcp-stdio';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
// Optional: Official transports if you prefer them
// import { StdioClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/stdio';
// import { SSEClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/sse';
// import { StreamableHTTPClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/streamableHttp';

let clientOne;
let clientTwo;
let clientThree;

try {
  // Initialize an MCP client to connect to a `stdio` MCP server (local only):
  const transport = new Experimental_StdioMCPTransport({
    command: 'node',
    args: ['src/stdio/dist/server.js'],
  });

  const clientOne = await createMCPClient({
    transport,
  });

  // Connect to an HTTP MCP server directly via the client transport config
  const clientTwo = await createMCPClient({
    transport: {
      type: 'http',
      url: 'http://localhost:3000/mcp',

      // optional: configure headers
      // headers: { Authorization: 'Bearer my-api-key' },

      // optional: provide an OAuth client provider for automatic authorization
      // authProvider: myOAuthClientProvider,
    },
  });

  // Connect to a Server-Sent Events (SSE) MCP server directly via the client transport config
  const clientThree = await createMCPClient({
    transport: {
      type: 'sse',
      url: 'http://localhost:3000/sse',

      // optional: configure headers
      // headers: { Authorization: 'Bearer my-api-key' },

      // optional: provide an OAuth client provider for automatic authorization
      // authProvider: myOAuthClientProvider,
    },
  });

  // Alternatively, you can create transports with the official SDKs instead of direct config:
  // const httpTransport = new StreamableHTTPClientTransport(new URL('http://localhost:3000/mcp'));
  // clientTwo = await createMCPClient({ transport: httpTransport });
  // const sseTransport = new SSEClientTransport(new URL('http://localhost:3000/sse'));
  // clientThree = await createMCPClient({ transport: sseTransport });

  const toolSetOne = await clientOne.tools();
  const toolSetTwo = await clientTwo.tools();
  const toolSetThree = await clientThree.tools();
  const tools = {
    ...toolSetOne,
    ...toolSetTwo,
    ...toolSetThree, // note: this approach causes subsequent tool sets to override tools with the same name
  };

  const response = await generateText({
    model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
    tools,
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    messages: [
      {
        role: 'user',
        content: [{ type: 'text', text: 'Find products under $100' }],
      },
    ],
  });

  console.log(response.text);
} catch (error) {
  console.error(error);
} finally {
  await Promise.all([
    clientOne.close(),
    clientTwo.close(),
    clientThree.close(),
  ]);
}
```

### Configure API Route with Single Tool and Step Limit

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

Set up a POST endpoint that uses streamText with the stopWhen condition to limit model steps to 5. Includes a weather tool that returns random temperature data for a given location. The endpoint converts UIMessages to model messages and returns a UI message stream response.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none',
    },
  });
}
```

### Enable Enhanced Reasoning with Thinking Mode

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gemini

Configure Gemini 3 to use enhanced reasoning through thinking mode to improve problem-solving capabilities. The thinkingLevel parameter controls reasoning depth, with different values supported by Gemini 3 Pro and Flash models.

```typescript
import { google, GoogleLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-3-pro-preview'),
  prompt: 'What is the sum of the first 10 prime numbers?',
  providerOptions: {
    google: {
      thinkingConfig: {
        includeThoughts: true,
        thinkingLevel: 'low',
      },
    } satisfies GoogleLanguageModelOptions,
  },
});

console.log(text);
```

### Dynamic Tool Configuration with User Location

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/configuring-call-options

Demonstrates configuring tools dynamically based on runtime context. The example shows how to pass user location information to a web search tool through call options, allowing location-aware search results.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

const newsAgent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  callOptionsSchema: z.object({
    userCity: z.string().optional(),
    userRegion: z.string().optional(),
  }),
  tools: {
    web_search: openai.tools.webSearch(),
  },
  prepareCall: ({ options, ...settings }) => ({
    ...settings,
    tools: {
      web_search: openai.tools.webSearch({
        searchContextSize: 'low',
        userLocation: {
          type: 'approximate',
          city: options.userCity,
          region: options.userRegion,
          country: 'US',
        },
      }),
    },
  }),
});

await newsAgent.generate({
  prompt: 'What are the top local news stories?',
  options: {
    userCity: 'San Francisco',
    userRegion: 'California',
  },
});
```

### Restoring AI State with initialAIState in AI SDK RSC

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-rsc/saving-and-restoring-states

This example shows how to restore the AI state when a component mounts by asynchronously loading chat history from a database and passing it to the `initialAIState` prop of the `AI` context provider. This ensures the application starts with the user's last known AI state.

```tsx
import { ReactNode } from 'react';
import { AI } from './ai';

export default async function RootLayout({
  children,
}: Readonly<{ children: ReactNode }>) {
  const chat = await loadChatFromDB();

  return (
    <html lang="en">
      <body>
        <AI initialAIState={chat}>{children}</AI>
      </body>
    </html>
  );
}
```

### Add Weather Tool to Agent with Multi-step Execution

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/deepseek-v3-2

Extend the chat route handler with a weather tool that the DeepSeek model can invoke. The tool accepts a location parameter and returns weather data. The stopWhen parameter enables multi-step agent execution (up to 5 steps) for iterative reasoning and tool use.

```typescript
import { deepseek } from '@ai-sdk/deepseek';
import {
  convertToModelMessages,
  stepCountIs,
  streamText,
  tool,
  UIMessage,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: deepseek('deepseek-reasoner'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => ({
          location,
          temperature: 72,
          unit: 'fahrenheit',
        }),
      }),
    },
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({ sendReasoning: true });
}
```

### Create Custom AI SDK Provider Entry Point in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/custom-providers

Shows how to set up the entry point for a custom AI SDK provider, including defining interfaces for the provider and its settings, and implementing a factory function (`createCustom`) to instantiate the provider and its language models. This snippet also demonstrates API key loading and base URL configuration.

```ts
import {
  generateId,
  loadApiKey,
  withoutTrailingSlash,
} from '@ai-sdk/provider-utils';
import { ProviderV3 } from '@ai-sdk/provider';
import { CustomChatLanguageModel } from './custom-chat-language-model';

// Define your provider interface extending ProviderV3
interface CustomProvider extends ProviderV3 {
  (modelId: string, settings?: CustomChatSettings): CustomChatLanguageModel;

  // Add specific methods for different model types
  languageModel(
    modelId: string,
    settings?: CustomChatSettings,
  ): CustomChatLanguageModel;
}

// Provider settings
interface CustomProviderSettings {
  /**
   * Base URL for API calls
   */
  baseURL?: string;

  /**
   * API key for authentication
   */
  apiKey?: string;

  /**
   * Custom headers for requests
   */
  headers?: Record<string, string>;
}

// Factory function to create provider instance
function createCustom(options: CustomProviderSettings = {}): CustomProvider {
  const createChatModel = (
    modelId: string,
    settings: CustomChatSettings = {},
  ) =>
    new CustomChatLanguageModel(modelId, settings, {
      provider: 'custom',
      baseURL:
        withoutTrailingSlash(options.baseURL) ?? 'https://api.custom.ai/v1',
      headers: () => ({
        Authorization: `Bearer ${loadApiKey({
          apiKey: options.apiKey,
          environmentVariableName: 'CUSTOM_API_KEY',
          description: 'Custom Provider',
        })}`,
        ...options.headers,
      }),
      generateId: options.generateId ?? generateId,
    });

  const provider = function (modelId: string, settings?: CustomChatSettings) {
    if (new.target) {
      throw new Error(
        'The model factory function cannot be called with the new keyword.',
      );
    }

    return createChatModel(modelId, settings);
  };

  provider.languageModel = createChatModel;

  return provider as CustomProvider;
}

// Export default provider instance
const custom = createCustom();
```

### Create AI Chat Route Handler with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Defines an asynchronous POST request handler for the `/api/chat` endpoint using the AI SDK. It processes `UIMessage` history from the request body, converts it to `ModelMessage` for the AI model, streams text responses, and returns them in a UI-compatible format.

```tsx
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Create API Route with AI SDK Gateway Provider

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nuxt

Sets up a Nuxt event handler that creates an AI Gateway instance, receives chat messages from the client, streams text responses using Anthropic Claude model, and returns the streamed response. The code demonstrates message conversion from UIMessage to ModelMessage format and proper error handling for missing API keys.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  createGateway,
} from 'ai';

export default defineLazyEventHandler(async () => {
  const apiKey = useRuntimeConfig().aiGatewayApiKey;
  if (!apiKey) throw new Error('Missing AI Gateway API key');
  const gateway = createGateway({
    apiKey: apiKey,
  });

  return defineEventHandler(async (event: any) => {
    const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await readBody(event);

    const result = streamText({
      model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
      messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    });

    return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
  });
});
```

### Configure NodeSDK with BraintrustSpanProcessor

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/observability/braintrust

Sets up OpenTelemetry NodeSDK with BraintrustSpanProcessor for Node.js applications. Initializes the SDK with span processors, starts it, and executes an AI function with tool calling and telemetry enabled. Includes example tools for listing orders and viewing tracking information with proper shutdown handling.

```typescript
import { NodeSDK } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-node';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { BraintrustSpanProcessor } from 'braintrust';

const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  spanProcessors: [
    new BraintrustSpanProcessor({
      parent: 'project_name:your-project-name',
      filterAISpans: true,
    }),
  ],
});

sdk.start();

async function main() {
  const result = await generateText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o-mini'),
    messages: [
      {
        role: 'user',
        content: 'What are my orders and where are they? My user ID is 123',
      },
    ],
    tools: {
      listOrders: tool({
        description: 'list all orders',
        parameters: z.object({ userId: z.string() }),
        execute: async ({ userId }) =>
          `User ${userId} has the following orders: 1`,
      }),
      viewTrackingInformation: tool({
        description: 'view tracking information for a specific order',
        parameters: z.object({ orderId: z.string() }),
        execute: async ({ orderId }) =>
          `Here is the tracking information for ${orderId}`,
      }),
    },
    experimental_telemetry: {
      isEnabled: true,
      functionId: 'my-awesome-function',
      metadata: {
        something: 'custom',
        someOtherThing: 'other-value',
      },
    },
    maxSteps: 10,
  });

  await sdk.shutdown();
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Configure Multi-Step Tool Calls with stopWhen in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

Update a TypeScript application to enable multi-step tool calls by configuring `stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)` in the `streamText` function. This allows the agent to perform up to 5 steps of generation and tool usage. The `onStepFinish` callback logs tool results from each step, enabling visibility into the agent's tool usage patterns.

```typescript
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');

    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: __MODEL__,
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');

    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Create Server Action to Generate Chart Configuration with AI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/natural-language-postgres

This TypeScript Server Action (`generateChartConfig`) takes SQL query results and a user's natural language query as input. It uses an AI model (OpenAI GPT-4o) to generate a chart configuration object based on the predefined `configSchema`. The action includes a system prompt for the AI, an example config, and dynamically overrides generated colors with `shadcn` theme colors for consistent styling. It handles potential errors during the generation process.

```ts
/* ...other imports... */
import { Config, configSchema, explanationsSchema, Result } from '@/lib/types';

/* ...rest of the file... */

export const generateChartConfig = async (
  results: Result[],
  userQuery: string,
) => {
  'use server';

  try {
    const { object: config } = await generateObject({
      model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
      system: 'You are a data visualization expert.',
      prompt: `Given the following data from a SQL query result, generate the chart config that best visualises the data and answers the users query.
      For multiple groups use multi-lines.

      Here is an example complete config:
      export const chartConfig = {
        type: "pie",
        xKey: "month",
        yKeys: ["sales", "profit", "expenses"],
        colors: {
          sales: "#4CAF50",    // Green for sales
          profit: "#2196F3",   // Blue for profit
          expenses: "#F44336"  // Red for expenses
        },
        legend: true
      }

      User Query:
      ${userQuery}

      Data:
      ${JSON.stringify(results, null, 2)}`,
      schema: configSchema,
    });

    // Override with shadcn theme colors
    const colors: Record<string, string> = {};
    config.yKeys.forEach((key, index) => {
      colors[key] = `hsl(var(--chart-${index + 1}))`;
    });

    const updatedConfig = { ...config, colors };
    return { config: updatedConfig };
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate chart suggestion');
  }
};
```
