### Implement useChat Hook with Message Display and Reasoning

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/r1

Create a Next.js client component using the useChat hook to manage chat state, handle form submissions, and display messages with reasoning tokens. The component renders different message parts (reasoning vs text) and provides an input form for user messages.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
              return <pre key={index}>{part.text}</pre>;
            }
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <span key={index}>{part.text}</span>;
            }
            return null;
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Integrate Model Context Protocol (MCP) Tool with AI SDK Responses API (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

This snippet demonstrates how to connect to remote Model Context Protocol (MCP) servers, allowing the model to utilize tools exposed by external services. It configures the `mcp` tool with `serverLabel`, `serverUrl`, and `serverDescription`.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-5-mini'),
  prompt: 'Search the web for the latest NYC mayoral election results',
  tools: {
    mcp: openai.tools.mcp({
      serverLabel: 'web-search',
      serverUrl: 'https://mcp.exa.ai/mcp',
      serverDescription: 'A web-search API for AI agents',
    }),
  },
});

console.log(result.text);
```

### Initialize and Use AI SDK MCP Client for Text Generation

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/create-mcp-client

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to set up an MCP client using `createMCPClient` with a `StdioMCPTransport` to communicate with a `node server.js` process. It shows how to retrieve tools from the client, integrate them into an `ai/generateText` call, and includes essential `try...catch...finally` blocks for error handling and ensuring proper client resource cleanup.

```typescript
import { createMCPClient } from '@ai-sdk/mcp';
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { Experimental_StdioMCPTransport } from '@ai-sdk/mcp/mcp-stdio';

let client;

try {
  client = await createMCPClient({
    transport: new Experimental_StdioMCPTransport({
      command: 'node server.js',
    }),
  });

  const tools = await client.tools();

  const response = await generateText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    tools,
    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: 'Query the data' }],
  });

  console.log(response);
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Error:', error);
} finally {
  // ensure the client is closed even if an error occurs
  if (client) {
    await client.close();
  }
}
```

### Create and use bash tools with AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/tools-registry/bash-tool

Initialize bash-tool with file system context and integrate it with AI SDK's generateText function. The example creates tools for bash execution, file reading, and writing, then uses them with Claude Sonnet 4 to list files and display contents.

```javascript
import { generateText, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { createBashTool } from 'bash-tool';

const { tools } = await createBashTool({
  files: { 'src/index.ts': "export const hello = 'world';" }
});

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: 'anthropic/claude-sonnet-4',
  prompt: 'List the files in src/ and show me the contents of index.ts',
  tools,
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5)
});

console.log(text);
```

### experimental_listPrompts

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/create-mcp-client

Lists available prompts from the MCP server. This method is experimental and may change in the future.

```APIDOC
## experimental_listPrompts

### Description
Lists available prompts from the MCP server. This method is experimental and may change in the future.

### Method
N/A (Client Method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **options** (object) - Optional - Configuration options for listing prompts.
  - **params** (PaginatedRequest['params']) - Optional - Optional pagination parameters including cursor.
  - **options** (RequestOptions) - Optional - Optional request options including signal and timeout.

### Request Example
{
  "options": {
    "params": {
      "limit": 5
    }
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_value** (Promise<ListPromptsResult>) - A promise that resolves to a list of available prompts.

#### Response Example
{
  "prompts": [
    { "name": "greeting", "version": "1.0" },
    { "name": "farewell", "version": "1.1" }
  ],
  "nextCursor": "prompt_page_token"
}
```

### Transcribe Audio with AssemblyAI and Advanced Provider Options in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/assemblyai

This example shows how to transcribe an audio file using the `experimental_transcribe` function with an AssemblyAI model. It includes reading an audio file and configuring provider-specific options, such as enabling `contentSafety`, through the `providerOptions` object for fine-grained control over the transcription process.

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { assemblyai } from '@ai-sdk/assemblyai';
import { type AssemblyAITranscriptionModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/assemblyai';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: assemblyai.transcription('best'),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: {
    assemblyai: {
      contentSafety: true,
    } satisfies AssemblyAITranscriptionModelOptions,
  },
});
```

```ts
function addToolInputExamplesMiddleware(options?: {

}): LanguageModelMiddleware;
```

### Build Chat UI with useChat Hook in Next.js

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gpt-5

Create a client-side chat interface using the useChat hook from AI SDK React. The component manages message state, displays conversation history with user and AI roles, and handles form submission to send new messages to the chat endpoint.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({});

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <span key={index}>{part.text}</span>;
            }
            return null;
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          if (input.trim()) {
            sendMessage({ text: input });
            setInput('');
          }
        }}
      >
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Implement Custom Tool Search Logic with AI SDK and Anthropic

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/anthropic

This example demonstrates how to implement custom tool search logic within the AI SDK using Anthropic models. It shows how to define a `searchTools` tool that filters available tools based on a query and uses `toModelOutput` to return `tool-reference` content blocks, allowing Anthropic to load deferred tool schemas dynamically.

```ts
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-5'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    // Custom search tool
    searchTools: tool({
      description: 'Search for tools by keyword',
      inputSchema: z.object({ query: z.string() }),
      execute: async ({ query }) => {
        // Your custom search logic (embeddings, fuzzy match, etc.)
        const allTools = ['get_weather', 'get_forecast', 'get_temperature'];
        return allTools.filter(name => name.includes(query.toLowerCase()));
      },
      toModelOutput: ({ output }) => ({
        type: 'content',
        value: (output as string[]).map(toolName => ({
          type: 'custom' as const,
          providerOptions: {
            anthropic: {
              type: 'tool-reference',
              toolName,
            },
          },
        })),
      }),
    }),

    // Deferred tools
    get_weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the current weather',
      inputSchema: z.object({ location: z.string() }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({ location, temperature: 72 }),
      providerOptions: {
        anthropic: { deferLoading: true },
      },
    }),
  },
});
```

### Configure Groq Reasoning Model Options with AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/groq

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to use the `@ai-sdk/groq` package to generate text with a Groq reasoning model. It showcases configuring various `providerOptions` such as `reasoningFormat`, `reasoningEffort`, `parallelToolCalls`, `user` identification, and `serviceTier` for fine-grained control over model behavior and performance.

```typescript
import { groq, type GroqLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: groq('qwen/qwen3-32b'),
  providerOptions: {
    groq: {
      reasoningFormat: 'parsed',
      reasoningEffort: 'default',
      parallelToolCalls: true, // Enable parallel function calling (default: true)
      user: 'user-123', // Unique identifier for end-user (optional)
      serviceTier: 'flex', // Use flex tier for higher throughput (optional)
    } satisfies GroqLanguageModelOptions,
  },
  prompt: 'How many "r"s are in the word "strawberry"?',
});
```

### Implement Tool Calling with Multi-Step Agent Behavior

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/openai-responses

Demonstrate tool calling with the AI SDK using the Responses API, enabling the model to autonomously call external tools, analyze results, and make additional calls. The stopWhen parameter with stepCountIs(5) transforms a single LLM call into a multi-step agent that can chain actions together.

```TypeScript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai.responses('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
});
```

### Integrate DeepSeek R1 via Fireworks with Reasoning Extraction

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/r1

This TypeScript code shows how to use DeepSeek R1 through the Fireworks provider within the AI SDK. It utilizes `wrapLanguageModel` and `extractReasoningMiddleware` to enhance the model, allowing for the extraction of internal reasoning tokens (tagged as 'think') alongside the final generated text.

```ts
import { fireworks } from '@ai-sdk/fireworks';
import {
  generateText,
  wrapLanguageModel,
  extractReasoningMiddleware,
} from 'ai';

// middleware to extract reasoning tokens
const enhancedModel = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: fireworks('accounts/fireworks/models/deepseek-r1'),
  middleware: extractReasoningMiddleware({ tagName: 'think' }),
});

const { reasoningText, text } = await generateText({
  model: enhancedModel,
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement.',
});
```

### Implement Multi-Step Agents with AI SDK for Problem Solving (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

This snippet demonstrates how to create an AI agent capable of multi-step reasoning and tool usage using the AI SDK's 'maxSteps' parameter. The agent is configured with a 'calculate' tool (using 'mathjs') to evaluate mathematical expressions. It solves a profit calculation problem by reasoning step-by-step and invoking the calculator tool as needed, showcasing dynamic decision-making.

```typescript
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import * as mathjs from 'mathjs';
import { z } from 'zod';

const problem =
  'Calculate the profit for a day if revenue is $5000 and expenses are $3500.';

const { text: answer } = await generateText({
  model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
  system:
    'You are solving math problems. Reason step by step. Use the calculator when necessary.',
  prompt: problem,
  tools: {
    calculate: tool({
      description: 'A tool for evaluating mathematical expressions.',
      inputSchema: z.object({ expression: z.string() }),
      execute: async ({ expression }) => mathjs.evaluate(expression),
    }),
  },
  maxSteps: 5,
});
```

### Apply Provider Options at Message Level (AI SDK)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/prompts

This example illustrates how to apply provider-specific options to individual messages within a message array using the `providerOptions` property. This allows for granular control, such as setting cache control for a specific system message (e.g., `cacheControl` for Anthropic), enabling fine-tuned behavior for different parts of a conversation.

```typescript
import { ModelMessage } from 'ai';

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [
  {
    role: 'system',
    content: 'Cached system message',
    providerOptions: {
      // Sets a cache control breakpoint on the system message
      anthropic: { cacheControl: { type: 'ephemeral' } },
    },
  },
];
```

### Create Chat API Route Handler with DeepSeek Streaming

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/r1

Create a Next.js route handler that accepts chat messages, streams responses from DeepSeek R1 model, and forwards reasoning tokens to the client. The handler converts UI messages to model format and returns a streamed response with reasoning enabled.

```typescript
import { deepseek } from '@ai-sdk/deepseek';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: deepseek('deepseek-reasoner'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

--------------------------------

### Stream Text with OpenAI o1 in Next.js API Route

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o1

Creates a POST endpoint that accepts chat messages, converts them to model format, and streams responses using OpenAI's o1 model. The endpoint allows responses up to 5 minutes duration and returns a UI-compatible message stream response.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow responses up to 5 minutes
export const maxDuration = 300;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('o1'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Configure Custom Body Fields Per Request in React Chat

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-ui/chatbot

Demonstrates a complete React chat component using useChat hook with custom body fields passed to sendMessage. The example shows how to submit a form with additional custom data (customKey) that gets sent to the backend API.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');

  return (
    <div>
      {messages.map(m => (
        <div key={m.id}>
          {m.role}:{' '}
          {m.parts.map((part, index) =>
            part.type === 'text' ? <span key={index}>{part.text}</span> : null,
          )}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={event => {
          event.preventDefault();
          if (input.trim()) {
            sendMessage(
              { text: input },
              {
                body: {
                  customKey: 'customValue',
                },
              },
            );
            setInput('');
          }
        }}
      >
        <input value={input} onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)} />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Create Server Action to Explain SQL Queries (Initial)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/natural-language-postgres

This TypeScript server action, `explainQuery`, is designed to generate explanations for SQL queries using an AI model. It accepts the original natural language input and the generated SQL query as parameters. The action utilizes the `generateObject` function with an OpenAI model and a system prompt (defined previously) to process the query, but initially lacks a defined output schema for the explanation structure.

```ts
/* ...rest of the file... */

export const explainQuery = async (input: string, sqlQuery: string) => {
  'use server';
  try {
    const result = await generateObject({
      model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
      system: `You are a SQL (postgres) expert. ...`, // SYSTEM PROMPT AS ABOVE - OMITTED FOR BREVITY
      prompt: `Explain the SQL query you generated to retrieve the data the user wanted. Assume the user is not an expert in SQL. Break down the query into steps. Be concise.

      User Query:
      ${input}

      Generated SQL Query:
      ${sqlQuery}`,
    });
    return result.object;
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate query');
  }
};
```

### Create Polyfills File for AI SDK in Expo

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

This TypeScript code creates a `polyfills.js` file that conditionally sets up `structuredClone`, `TextEncoderStream`, and `TextDecoderStream` polyfills for non-web platforms within an Expo project. It imports necessary modules and uses `polyfillGlobal` from `react-native` to make these functions available globally.

```typescript
import { Platform } from 'react-native';
import structuredClone from '@ungap/structured-clone';

if (Platform.OS !== 'web') {
  const setupPolyfills = async () => {
    const { polyfillGlobal } = await import(
      'react-native/Libraries/Utilities/PolyfillFunctions'
    );

    const { TextEncoderStream, TextDecoderStream } = await import(
      '@stardazed/streams-text-encoding'
    );

    if (!('structuredClone' in global)) {
      polyfillGlobal('structuredClone', () => structuredClone);
    }

    polyfillGlobal('TextEncoderStream', () => TextEncoderStream);
    polyfillGlobal('TextDecoderStream', () => TextDecoderStream);
  };

  setupPolyfills();
}

export {};
```

### Configure Multi-Step `generateText` with `stopWhen` and Tools (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/tools-and-tool-calling

This example demonstrates how to use `generateText` with the `stopWhen` setting to enable multi-step calls. The model is provided with a 'weather' tool and a stopping condition (`stepCountIs(5)`), allowing it to call the tool and then generate a response based on the tool's output. This setup facilitates scenarios where the model needs to perform an action before providing a final text response.

```typescript
import { z } from 'zod';
import { generateText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

const { text, steps } = await generateText({
  model: __MODEL__,
  tools: {
    weather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(5), // stop after a maximum of 5 steps if tools were called
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
});
```

### Implementing Eager Stream Processing with JavaScript Generators and ReadableStream

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/advanced/backpressure

This example demonstrates an eager approach to streaming data using an async generator and a `ReadableStream`. It illustrates how a generator can produce data much faster than a consumer can process it, leading to an ever-expanding internal buffer within the stream. The `start` handler of the `ReadableStream` eagerly enqueues values from the generator without respecting back-pressure from the consumer.

```javascript
// A generator that will yield positive integers
async function* integers() {
  let i = 1;
  while (true) {
    console.log(`yielding ${i}`);
    yield i++;

    await sleep(100);
  }
}
function sleep(ms) {
  return new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
}

// Wraps a generator into a ReadableStream
function createStream(iterator) {
  return new ReadableStream({
    async start(controller) {
      for await (const v of iterator) {
        controller.enqueue(v);
      }
      controller.close();
    },
  });
}

// Collect data from stream
async function run() {
  // Set up a stream of integers
  const stream = createStream(integers());

  // Read values from our stream
  const reader = stream.getReader();
  for (let i = 0; i < 10_000; i++) {
    // we know our stream is infinite, so there's no need to check `done`.
    const { value } = await reader.read();
    console.log(`read ${value}`);

    await sleep(1_000);
  }
}
run();
```

### Configure AI SDK `generateText` reasoning effort with OpenAI 'o1' model

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o1

This snippet demonstrates how to control the computational effort the 'o1' model expends on internal reasoning using the `reasoningEffort` parameter. Setting it to 'low' can result in faster responses, while 'high' might lead to more thorough but slower processing. This parameter is specific to the 'o1' model.

```ts
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

// Reduce reasoning effort for faster responses
const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o1'),
  prompt: 'Explain quantum entanglement briefly.',
  providerOptions: {
    openai: { reasoningEffort: 'low' },
  },
});
```

### Send custom data with AI SDK UI message stream in Fastify (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/api-servers/fastify

This example illustrates how to send custom data alongside AI-generated content using `createUIMessageStream` in a Fastify server. It allows for writing custom events (like 'start' or 'data-custom') before merging with the AI SDK's `toUIMessageStream`, providing fine-grained control over the streamed output.

```ts
import { createUIMessageStream, streamText } from 'ai';
import Fastify from 'fastify';

const fastify = Fastify({ logger: true });

fastify.post('/stream-data', async function (request, reply) {
  // immediately start streaming the response
  const stream = createUIMessageStream({
    execute: async ({ writer }) => {
      writer.write({ type: 'start' });

      writer.write({
        type: 'data-custom',
        data: {
          custom: 'initialized call',
        },
      });

      const result = streamText({
        model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
        prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
      });

      writer.merge(result.toUIMessageStream({ sendStart: false }));
    },
    onError: error => {
      // Error messages are masked by default for security reasons.
      // If you want to expose the error message to the client, you can do so here:
      return error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error);
    },
  });

  reply.header('Content-Type', 'text/plain; charset=utf-8');

  return reply.send(stream);
});

fastify.listen({ port: 8080 });
```

### Frontend Component Calling Server Action with streamComponent

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

Shows how to call a Server Action from a client component using 'use client' directive. The component manages state for the streamed React component and handles form submission to trigger the streamComponent Server Action, displaying the returned component in the UI.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useState } from 'react';
import { streamComponent } from './actions';

export default function Page() {
  const [component, setComponent] = useState<React.ReactNode>();

  return (
    <div>
      <form
        onSubmit={async e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          setComponent(await streamComponent());
        }}
      >
        <button>Stream Component</button>
      </form>
      <div>{component}</div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### tools

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/create-mcp-client

Gets the tools available from the MCP server.

```APIDOC
## tools

### Description
Gets the tools available from the MCP server.

### Method
N/A (Client Method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **options** (object) - Optional - Configuration options for retrieving tools.
  - **schemas** (TOOL_SCHEMAS) - Optional - Schema definitions for compile-time type checking. When not provided, schemas are inferred from the server. Each tool schema can include inputSchema for typed inputs, and optionally outputSchema for typed outputs when the server returns structuredContent.
- **TOOL_SCHEMAS** (object) - Required - Defines the structure for tool schemas.
  - **inputSchema** (FlexibleSchema) - Required - Zod schema or JSON schema defining the expected input parameters for the tool.
  - **outputSchema** (FlexibleSchema) - Optional - Zod schema or JSON schema defining the expected output structure. When provided, the client extracts and validates structuredContent from tool results, giving you typed outputs.

### Request Example
{
  "options": {
    "schemas": {
      "myTool": {
        "inputSchema": { "type": "object", "properties": { "query": { "type": "string" } } },
        "outputSchema": { "type": "object", "properties": { "result": { "type": "string" } } }
      }
    }
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_value** (Promise<McpToolSet<TOOL_SCHEMAS>>) - A promise that resolves to an object containing the available tools, typed according to the provided schemas.

#### Response Example
{
  // Example would depend on actual tool definitions and server response.
  // e.g., { "myTool": { "run": async (args) => { ... } } }
}
```

### Configure LangSmithDeploymentTransport for AI SDK useChat Hook

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/adapters/langchain

This example demonstrates the configuration of `LangSmithDeploymentTransport` for use with the `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react`. It shows how to instantiate the transport with a LangSmith deployment URL and an optional API key, ensuring efficient creation using `useMemo`. This setup enables direct communication from the client to a LangGraph deployment.

```ts
import { LangSmithDeploymentTransport } from '@ai-sdk/langchain';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useMemo } from 'react';

const transport = useMemo(
  ()
    =>
    new LangSmithDeploymentTransport({
      url: 'https://your-deployment.us.langgraph.app',
      apiKey: 'your-api-key',
    }),
  [],
);

const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
  transport,
});
```

### Create Next.js API Route for AI Chat Streaming (TypeScript/TSX)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o3

This Next.js API route (`app/api/chat/route.ts`) handles incoming chat messages, converts them to a model-compatible format, and streams responses from an OpenAI model using `streamText`. It's designed to provide real-time chat interactions for frontend applications built with AI SDK UI.

```tsx
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow responses up to 5 minutes
export const maxDuration = 300;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('o3-mini'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Integrate custom tools with AI SDK `generateText` for enhanced capabilities

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/o1

This snippet demonstrates how to extend the capabilities of the 'o1' model by integrating custom tools with the `generateText` function. By defining a tool with an input schema and an `execute` function, the model can perform discrete tasks or interact with external systems, such as fetching real-time weather data. This allows LLMs to overcome limitations in areas like mathematics or external world interaction.

```ts
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: openai('o1'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather like today?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        location,
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10,
      }),
    }),
  },
});
```

### Define Next.js API Route for AI Chat Streaming (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/sonnet-3-7

This TypeScript route handler (`app/api/chat/route.ts`) processes incoming chat requests. It leverages `streamText` from AI SDK with the Anthropic model to generate and stream AI responses, converting UI messages and optionally sending reasoning tokens.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { streamText, convertToModelMessages, type UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    providerOptions: {
      anthropic: {
        thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 12000 },
      } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

### Transcribe Audio with Fal AI SDK and Custom Options (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/fal

This example shows how to perform an audio transcription using the `experimental_transcribe` function from the AI SDK, integrating with Fal's transcription model. It demonstrates passing an audio file and custom `providerOptions` like `batchSize` to Fal, allowing for parallel processing of audio chunks. The `readFile` function is used to load the audio content.

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { fal, type FalTranscriptionModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/fal';
import { readFile } from 'fs/promises';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: fal.transcription('wizper'),
  audio: await readFile('audio.mp3'),
  providerOptions: {
    fal: { batchSize: 10 } satisfies FalTranscriptionModelOptions,
  },
});
```

### Install OpenTelemetry Dependencies

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/observability/axiom

```typescript
const result = await generateText({
```

### Integrate Local Caching Middleware with AI SDK StreamText (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/node/local-caching-middleware

This TypeScript example shows how to use a local caching middleware (`cached`) with the AI SDK's `streamText` function. It imports necessary modules, wraps an OpenAI model with the caching layer, and then streams the generated text, logging token usage and finish reason. This setup is primarily intended for local development to reduce API calls during testing.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { cached } from '../middleware/your-cache-middleware';

async function main() {
  const result = streamText({
    model: cached(openai('gpt-4o')),
    maxOutputTokens: 512,
    temperature: 0.3,
    maxRetries: 5,
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  });

  for await (const textPart of result.textStream) {
    process.stdout.write(textPart);
  }

  console.log();
  console.log('Token usage:', await result.usage);
  console.log('Finish reason:', await result.finishReason);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Send Dynamic Message Metadata from AI SDK Server-Side (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-ui/message-metadata

This example illustrates how to send message-level metadata from the server during a streaming response using the `messageMetadata` callback in `toUIMessageStreamResponse`. It shows how to attach different metadata (e.g., `createdAt`, `model`, `totalTokens`) at various stages of the stream, such as `start` and `finish`. This allows for dynamic tracking of message attributes throughout its lifecycle.

```ts
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import type { MyUIMessage } from '@/types';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: MyUIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages)
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    originalMessages: messages, // pass this in for type-safe return objects
    messageMetadata: ({ part }) => {
      // Send metadata when streaming starts
      if (part.type === 'start') {
        return {
          createdAt: Date.now(),
          model: 'your-model-id'
        };
      }

      // Send additional metadata when streaming completes
      if (part.type === 'finish') {
        return {
          totalTokens: part.totalUsage.totalTokens
        };
      }
    }
  });
}
```

### SQL Query Generation Prompt for Unicorns Database

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/natural-language-postgres

This prompt provides a large language model with detailed instructions for generating SQL (Postgres) queries for a 'unicorns' database. It includes the table schema, rules for string matching (LOWER/ILIKE), handling specific fields like 'select_investors', data interpretation (valuation, rates), and output formatting to ensure chart-friendly, quantitative results with at least two columns.

```txt
You are a SQL (postgres) and data visualization expert. Your job is to help the user write a SQL query to retrieve the data they need. The table schema is as follows:

unicorns (
  id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  company VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  valuation DECIMAL(10, 2) NOT NULL,
  date_joined DATE,
  country VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  city VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  industry VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  select_investors TEXT NOT NULL
);

Only retrieval queries are allowed.

For things like industry, company names and other string fields, use the ILIKE operator and convert both the search term and the field to lowercase using LOWER() function. For example: LOWER(industry) ILIKE LOWER('%search_term%').

Note: select_investors is a comma-separated list of investors. Trim whitespace to ensure you're grouping properly. Note, some fields may be null or have only one value.
When answering questions about a specific field, ensure you are selecting the identifying column (ie. what is Vercel's valuation would select company and valuation').

The industries available are:
- healthcare & life sciences
- consumer & retail
- financial services
- enterprise tech
- insurance
- media & entertainment
- industrials
- health

If the user asks for a category that is not in the list, infer based on the list above.

Note: valuation is in billions of dollars so 10b would be 10.0.
Note: if the user asks for a rate, return it as a decimal. For example, 0.1 would be 10%.

If the user asks for 'over time' data, return by year.

When searching for UK or USA, write out United Kingdom or United States respectively.

EVERY QUERY SHOULD RETURN QUANTITATIVE DATA THAT CAN BE PLOTTED ON A CHART! There should always be at least two columns. If the user asks for a single column, return the column and the count of the column. If the user asks for a rate, return the rate as a decimal. For example, 0.1 would be 10%.
```

### Define AI System Prompt for SQL Query Explanation

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/natural-language-postgres

This text-based prompt guides an AI model to act as a SQL (PostgreSQL) expert, explaining generated SQL queries to users. It instructs the model to break down queries into unique, logical sections and provide concise explanations for each, even if an explanation is empty. The prompt includes a database schema for context, enabling the AI to understand the data structure.

```txt
You are a SQL (postgres) expert. Your job is to explain to the user the SQL query you wrote to retrieve the data they asked for. The table schema is as follows:
unicorns (
  id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  company VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
  valuation DECIMAL(10, 2) NOT NULL,
  date_joined DATE,
  country VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  city VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  industry VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
  select_investors TEXT NOT NULL
);

When you explain you must take a section of the query, and then explain it. Each "section" should be unique. So in a query like: "SELECT * FROM unicorns limit 20", the sections could be "SELECT *", "FROM UNICORNS", "LIMIT 20".
If a section doesn't have any explanation, include it, but leave the explanation empty.
```

### Integrate Prompt Caching with generateText and prepareStep

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/node/dynamic-prompt-caching

Configure an agent using generateText with the prepareStep callback to apply cache control to messages. This example demonstrates setting up tools like analyzeFile and using the addCacheControlToMessages utility to optimize caching for Anthropic models. The maxSteps parameter controls the maximum number of agent iterations.

```typescript
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { addCacheControlToMessages } from './add-cache-control-to-messages';

async function main() {
  const result = await generateText({
    model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-5'),
    prompt: 'Help me analyze this codebase and suggest improvements.',
    maxSteps: 10,
    tools: {
      analyzeFile: tool({
        description: 'Analyze a file in the codebase',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          path: z.string().describe('Path to the file'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ path }) => {
          return { analysis: `Analysis of ${path}` };
        },
      }),
    },
    prepareStep: ({ messages, model }) => ({
      messages: addCacheControlToMessages({ messages, model }),
    }),
  });

  console.log(result.text);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Stream Custom Data and AI Text in Hono

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/examples/api-servers/hono

This Hono server example demonstrates how to combine custom data streaming with AI text streaming. It uses `createUIMessageStream` to send initial custom data (`type: 'start'`, `type: 'data-custom'`) and then merges an AI-generated text stream (inventing a holiday) into the same UI message stream. Error handling for the AI stream is also shown, allowing the error message to be exposed to the client. Ensure `AI_GATEWAY_API_KEY` is set.

```typescript
import { serve } from '@hono/node-server';
import {
  createUIMessageStream,
  createUIMessageStreamResponse,
  streamText,
} from 'ai';
import { Hono } from 'hono';

const app = new Hono();

app.post('/stream-data', async c => {
  // immediately start streaming the response
  const stream = createUIMessageStream({
    execute: ({ writer }) => {
      writer.write({ type: 'start' });

      writer.write({
        type: 'data-custom',
        data: {
          custom: 'Hello, world!',
        },
      });

      const result = streamText({
        model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
        prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
      });

      writer.merge(
        result.toUIMessageStream({
          sendStart: false,
          onError: error => {
            // Error messages are masked by default for security reasons.
            // If you want to expose the error message to the client, you can do so here:
            return error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error);
          },
        }),
      );
    },
  });
  return createUIMessageStreamResponse({ stream });
});

serve({ fetch: app.fetch, port: 8080 });
```

### Build Chat UI with useChat Hook in Next.js

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

Frontend React component that implements a chat interface using the useChat hook from AI SDK UI. Manages user input state, displays message history with role differentiation, and handles form submission to send messages to the backend API endpoint.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <span key={index}>{part.text}</span>;
            }
            return null;
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Submit</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Create UI Message Stream with Text and Merged Content

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-ui/create-ui-message-stream

Create a UI message stream that writes text messages with start, delta, and end chunks, then merges content from another stream. The example demonstrates proper message ID consistency across chunks and integration with streamText results. Includes error handling and finish callbacks for stream completion.

```typescript
const existingMessages: UIMessage[] = [
  /* ... */
];

const stream = createUIMessageStream({
  async execute({ writer }) {
    // Start a text message
    // Note: The id must be consistent across text-start, text-delta, and text-end steps
    // This allows the system to correctly identify they belong to the same text block
    writer.write({
      type: 'text-start',
      id: 'example-text',
    });

    // Write a message chunk
    writer.write({
      type: 'text-delta',
      id: 'example-text',
      delta: 'Hello',
    });

    // End the text message
    writer.write({
      type: 'text-end',
      id: 'example-text',
    });

    // Merge another stream from streamText
    const result = streamText({
      model: __MODEL__,
      prompt: 'Write a haiku about AI',
    });

    writer.merge(result.toUIMessageStream());
  },
  onError: error => `Custom error: ${error.message}`,
  originalMessages: existingMessages,
  onFinish: ({ messages, isContinuation, responseMessage }) => {
    console.log('Stream finished with messages:', messages);
  },
});
```

### Stream Text with DeepInfra in Next.js API Route

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/llama-3_1

Backend API route that handles chat messages using AI SDK's streamText function with DeepInfra's Llama 3.1 model. Converts incoming messages to model format and returns a streamed UI response. Includes a 30-second timeout for streaming responses.

```typescript
import { deepinfra } from '@ai-sdk/deepinfra';
import { convertToModelMessages, streamText, UIMessage } from 'ai';

// Allow streaming responses up to 30 seconds
export const maxDuration = 30;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: deepinfra('meta-llama/Meta-Llama-3.1-70B-Instruct'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Implement Next.js Chat UI with AI SDK useChat Hook (React/TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/sonnet-3-7

This React component (`app/page.tsx`) creates the frontend chat interface. It utilizes the `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react` to manage chat state, send messages to the API, and display streamed AI responses, including user input and AI reasoning parts.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({ api: '/api/chat' }),
  });

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id}>
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
            // text parts:
            if (part.type === 'text') {
              return <div key={index}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
            // reasoning parts:
            if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
              return <pre key={index}>{part.text}</pre>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
        />
        <button type="submit">Send</button>
      </form>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Perform Basic Web Search with AI SDK `generateText` and Perplexity in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/ai-gateway

This example demonstrates the fundamental usage of the Perplexity Search tool with the AI SDK's `generateText` function. It shows how to import the necessary modules, define a prompt, and attach the `perplexity_search` tool to enable web search capabilities for the AI model, logging the generated text, tool calls, and results.

```ts
import { gateway, generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-5-nano',
  prompt: 'Search for news about AI regulations in January 2025.',
  tools: {
    perplexity_search: gateway.tools.perplexitySearch(),
  },
});

console.log(result.text);
console.log('Tool calls:', JSON.stringify(result.toolCalls, null, 2));
console.log('Tool results:', JSON.stringify(result.toolResults, null, 2));
```

### Configure Computer Tool with AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/computer-use

Sets up the Computer Tool using Anthropic's provider-defined-client tools with display dimensions and execute function. The execute function handles screenshot capture and computer actions like mouse movements and clicks, with toModelOutput converting responses to model-compatible format.

```typescript
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { getScreenshot, executeComputerAction } from '@/utils/computer-use';

const computerTool = anthropic.tools.computer_20250124({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: getScreenshot(),
        };
      }
      default: {
        return executeComputerAction(action, coordinate, text);
      }
    }
  },
  toModelOutput({ output }) {
    return typeof output === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: output }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: output.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Implement Interactive Chat UI with AI SDK useChat Hook in Next.js (React/TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gemini

This React component, designed for a Next.js application, demonstrates how to create a dynamic chat interface using the AI SDK's `useChat` hook. It manages user input, sends messages to the backend API, and displays real-time AI responses, including handling different message content types.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'Gemini: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Perform Inpainting (Insert Objects) with Google Vertex Imagen 3.0 in AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-vertex

This example illustrates how to perform inpainting, specifically inserting objects, using the Google Vertex Imagen 3.0 model. It takes an input image and a mask (where white indicates the edit area) to guide the insertion of new elements based on a text prompt. The `providerOptions.vertex.edit` configuration specifies the inpainting mode and mask handling.

```typescript
import { vertex, GoogleVertexImageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/google-vertex';
import { generateImage } from 'ai';
import fs from 'fs';

const image = fs.readFileSync('./input-image.png');
const mask = fs.readFileSync('./mask.png'); // White = edit area

const { images } = await generateImage({
  model: vertex.image('imagen-3.0-capability-001'),
  prompt: {
    text: 'A sunlit indoor lounge area with a pool containing a flamingo',
    images: [image],
    mask,
  },
  providerOptions: {
    vertex: {
      edit: {
        baseSteps: 50,
        mode: 'EDIT_MODE_INPAINT_INSERTION',
        maskMode: 'MASK_MODE_USER_PROVIDED',
        maskDilation: 0.01,
      },
    } satisfies GoogleVertexImageModelOptions,
  },
});
```

### Build Chat UI with useChat Hook and Reasoning Display

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/claude-4

Create a React client component that implements a chat interface using the useChat hook from AI SDK. This component displays messages with role-based styling, handles user input submission, and renders model reasoning tokens in collapsible details elements. It connects to the chat API endpoint and manages message state automatically.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Page() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({ api: '/api/chat' }),
  });

  const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (input.trim()) {
      sendMessage({ text: input });
      setInput('');
    }
  };

  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col h-screen max-w-2xl mx-auto p-4">
      <div className="flex-1 overflow-y-auto space-y-4 mb-4">
        {messages.map(message => (
          <div
            key={message.id}
            className={`p-3 rounded-lg ${
              message.role === 'user' ? 'bg-blue-50 ml-auto' : 'bg-gray-50'
            }`}
          >
            <p className="font-semibold">
              {message.role === 'user' ? 'You' : 'Claude 4'}
            </p>
            {message.parts.map((part, index) => {
              if (part.type === 'text') {
                return (
                  <div key={index} className="mt-1">
                    {part.text}
                  </div>
                );
              }
              if (part.type === 'reasoning') {
                return (
                  <pre
                    key={index}
                    className="bg-gray-100 p-2 rounded mt-2 text-xs overflow-x-auto"
                  >
                    <details>
                      <summary className="cursor-pointer">
                        View reasoning
                      </summary>
                      {part.text}
                    </details>
                  </pre>
                );
              }
            })}
          </div>
        ))}
      </div>
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="flex gap-2">
        <input
          name="prompt"
          value={input}
          onChange={e => setInput(e.target.value)}
          className="flex-1 p-2 border rounded focus:outline-none focus:ring-2 focus:ring-blue-500"
          placeholder="Ask Claude 4 something..."
        />
        <button
          type="submit"
          className="bg-blue-500 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-blue-600"
        >
          Send
        </button>
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Generate Text with Audio Input using AI SDK and OpenAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/prompts

This snippet demonstrates how to use the `@ai-sdk/openai` package to generate text from an audio file. It reads an MP3 file from the local filesystem using `fs.readFileSync` and passes it as `audio/mpeg` content within the user message to the `generateText` function, allowing the model to process the audio.

```javascript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-4o-audio-preview'),
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        { type: 'text', text: 'What is the audio saying?' },
        {
          type: 'file',
          mediaType: 'audio/mpeg',
          data: fs.readFileSync('./data/galileo.mp3'),
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Enable Extended Thinking with Claude 3.7 Sonnet

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/sonnet-3-7

Enables Claude 3.7 Sonnet's extended thinking capability for complex reasoning tasks. Uses the `thinking` provider option with a configurable token budget to control reasoning depth. Returns reasoning text, reasoning details, and final text response for multi-step problem solving.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoningText, reasoning } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219'),
  prompt: 'How many people will live in the world in 2040?',
  providerOptions: {
    anthropic: {
      thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 12000 },
    } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
  },
});

console.log(reasoningText); // reasoning text
console.log(reasoning); // reasoning details including redacted reasoning
console.log(text); // text response
```

### Combine Multiple Server-Side Tools with xAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/xai

Demonstrates how to integrate multiple server-side tools including web search, X search, code execution, file search, and MCP servers in a single streamText request. The example processes the response stream and logs text deltas and URL sources. Requires grok-4-fast model and the Responses API.

```typescript
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const { fullStream } = streamText({
  model: xai.responses('grok-4-fast'),
  prompt: 'Research AI safety developments and calculate risk metrics',
  tools: {
    web_search: xai.tools.webSearch(),
    x_search: xai.tools.xSearch(),
    code_execution: xai.tools.codeExecution(),
    file_search: xai.tools.fileSearch({
      vectorStoreIds: ['collection_your-documents'],
    }),
    data_service: xai.tools.mcpServer({
      serverUrl: 'https://data.example.com/mcp',
      serverLabel: 'data-service',
    }),
  },
});

for await (const part of fullStream) {
  if (part.type === 'text-delta') {
    process.stdout.write(part.text);
  } else if (part.type === 'source' && part.sourceType === 'url') {
    console.log('\nSource:', part.url);
  }
}
```

### Basic Call Options with User Context

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/configuring-call-options

Demonstrates how to define a callOptionsSchema with user context fields and use prepareCall to inject user information into the agent's instructions. The options parameter becomes type-checked and required when calling generate().

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

const supportAgent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  callOptionsSchema: z.object({
    userId: z.string(),
    accountType: z.enum(['free', 'pro', 'enterprise']),
  }),
  instructions: 'You are a helpful customer support agent.',
  prepareCall: ({ options, ...settings }) => ({
    ...settings,
    instructions:
      settings.instructions +
      `\nUser context:
- Account type: ${options.accountType}
- User ID: ${options.userId}

Adjust your response based on the user's account level.`,
  }),
});

// Call the agent with specific user context
const result = await supportAgent.generate({
  prompt: 'How do I upgrade my account?',
  options: {
    userId: 'user_123',
    accountType: 'free',
  },
});
```

### Enable Live Search with Auto Mode in xAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/xai

Demonstrates how to enable Live Search functionality with auto mode, allowing the model to decide whether to search. The example retrieves text and sources from the response, with search configured to return citations and limit results to 5 items.

```typescript
import { xai, type XaiLanguageModelChatOptions } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources } = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in AI?',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'auto', // 'auto', 'on', or 'off'
        returnCitations: true,
        maxSearchResults: 5,
      },
    } satisfies XaiLanguageModelChatOptions,
  },
});

console.log(text);
console.log('Sources:', sources);
```

### Perform Web Search with Valyu AI SDK and AI model

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/tools-registry/valyu

This JavaScript example illustrates how to integrate Valyu's webSearch tool with an AI model (e.g., Google Gemini) to generate text based on real-time web information. It imports necessary modules, configures the webSearch tool, and uses it within a generateText call to answer prompts.

```javascript
import { generateText, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import { webSearch } from '@valyu/ai-sdk';
// Available specialised search tools: financeSearch, paperSearch,
// bioSearch, patentSearch, secSearch, economicsSearch, companyResearch

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: 'google/gemini-3-pro-preview',
  prompt: 'Latest data center projects for AI inference?',
  tools: {
    webSearch: webSearch()
  },
  stopWhen: stepCountIs(3)
});

console.log(text);
```

### Implement Tool Calling with Cencori and AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/cencori

Demonstrates how to use Cencori with the AI SDK for tool calling, allowing the model to execute predefined functions based on the prompt. This example defines a `getWeather` tool and shows how the model can invoke it to retrieve information.

```typescript
import { cencori } from 'cencori/vercel';
import { generateText, tool } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const { text, toolCalls } = await generateText({
  model: cencori('gpt-4o'),
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?',
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather for a location',
      parameters: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The city and state')
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => {
        return { temperature: 72, condition: 'sunny', location };
      }
    })
  }
});

console.log(text, toolCalls);
```

### Define Next.js API Route for AI Chat Endpoint (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/gemini

This TypeScript code sets up a Next.js API route (`POST /api/chat`) to handle chat requests. It leverages the AI SDK's `streamText` function with the Google Gemini 3 Pro model to process user messages and stream AI-generated text responses back to the client.

```typescript
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: google('gemini-3-pro-preview'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### experimental_getPrompt

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/create-mcp-client

Retrieves a prompt by name, optionally passing arguments. This method is experimental and may change in the future.

```APIDOC
## experimental_getPrompt

### Description
Retrieves a prompt by name, optionally passing arguments. This method is experimental and may change in the future.

### Method
N/A (Client Method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **args** (object) - Required - Arguments for retrieving a prompt.
  - **name** (string) - Required - The name of the prompt.
  - **arguments** (Record<string, unknown>) - Optional - Optional arguments to pass to the prompt.
  - **options** (RequestOptions) - Optional - Optional request options including signal and timeout.

### Request Example
{
  "args": {
    "name": "welcome_message",
    "arguments": {
      "user": "Alice",
      "language": "en"
    },
    "options": {
      "timeout": 2000
    }
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_value** (Promise<GetPromptResult>) - A promise that resolves to the retrieved prompt's content or structure.

#### Response Example
{
  "name": "welcome_message",
  "content": "Hello Alice, welcome to our service!",
  "version": "1.0"
}
```

### Create Streamable UI with render function using OpenAI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/migration-guides/migration-guide-3-1

Demonstrates the legacy render function approach for creating streamable UIs with OpenAI models. This example creates a Server Action that uses the render function with an OpenAI provider instance and defines a tool that returns a React Server Component for weather information.

```typescript
import { render } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import OpenAI from 'openai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { Spinner, Weather } from '@/components';
import { getWeather } from '@/utils';

const openai = new OpenAI();

async function submitMessage(userInput = 'What is the weather in SF?') {
  'use server';

  return render({
    provider: openai,
    model: 'gpt-4.1',
    messages: [
      { role: 'system', content: 'You are a helpful assistant' },
      { role: 'user', content: userInput },
    ],
    text: ({ content }) => <p>{content}</p>,
    tools: {
      get_city_weather: {
        description: 'Get the current weather for a city',
        parameters: z
          .object({
            city: z.string().describe('the city'),
          })
          .required(),
        render: async function* ({ city }) {
          yield <Spinner />;
          const weather = await getWeather(city);
          return <Weather info={weather} />;
        },
      },
    },
  });
}
```

### Configure Multi-Step Tool Calls with stopWhen in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Updates a Next.js API route handler to enable multi-step tool calls using the stopWhen condition set to stepCountIs(5). Includes a weather tool that returns temperature data and an onStepFinish callback to log tool results. The model can now use tool outputs to trigger additional generations up to 5 steps.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
    onStepFinish: ({ toolResults }) => {
      console.log(toolResults);
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Implement Chat UI with AI SDK `useChat` Hook in Next.js

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

This TypeScript React component (`app/page.tsx`) sets up a basic chat interface. It utilizes the `@ai-sdk/react` `useChat` hook to manage chat state, display messages, and send user input to an LLM backend (defaulting to `/api/chat`). It uses `useState` for local input management and renders messages, distinguishing between user and AI roles.

```tsx
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Create Chat API Route Handler with Streaming and Reasoning

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/claude-4

Set up a Next.js API route that handles POST requests for chat messages. This handler uses the Anthropic provider to stream text responses from Claude Sonnet 4, with support for interleaved thinking and reasoning tokens. It converts UI messages to model messages and returns a streamed response with optional reasoning data.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { streamText, convertToModelMessages, type UIMessage } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-20250514'),
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    headers: {
      'anthropic-beta': 'interleaved-thinking-2025-05-14',
    },
    providerOptions: {
      anthropic: {
        thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 15000 },
      } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    sendReasoning: true,
  });
}
```

### Combine Multiple Search Sources with XAI Model in AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/xai

This example demonstrates how to combine multiple search sources (web, news, X) in a single query using the AI SDK with an XAI model. It also shows how to enable citation returns and set a maximum number of search results. The `generateText` function queries the `grok-3-latest` model for a comprehensive overview.

```typescript
import { xai, type XaiLanguageModelChatOptions } from '@ai-sdk/xai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'Comprehensive overview of recent AI breakthroughs',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'on',
        returnCitations: true,
        maxSearchResults: 15,
        sources: [
          {
            type: 'web',
            allowedWebsites: ['arxiv.org', 'openai.com'],
          },
          {
            type: 'news',
            country: 'US',
          },
          {
            type: 'x',
            includedXHandles: ['openai', 'deepmind'],
          },
        ],
      },
    } satisfies XaiLanguageModelChatOptions,
  },
});
```

### Basic Usage Example of InferUITools with Zod

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-ui/infer-ui-tools

This example demonstrates how to define a `ToolSet` with `zod` schemas for tool inputs and then use `InferUITools` to automatically derive the precise TypeScript types for each tool's input and output. This ensures type safety when interacting with the defined tools.

```tsx
import { InferUITools } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const tools = {
  weather: {
    description: 'Get the current weather',
    inputSchema: z.object({
      location: z.string().describe('The city and state'),
    }),
    execute: async ({ location }) => {
      return `The weather in ${location} is sunny.`;
    },
  },
  calculator: {
    description: 'Perform basic arithmetic',
    inputSchema: z.object({
      operation: z.enum(['add', 'subtract', 'multiply', 'divide']),
      a: z.number(),
      b: z.number(),
    }),
    execute: async ({ operation, a, b }) => {
      switch (operation) {
        case 'add':
          return a + b;
        case 'subtract':
          return a - b;
        case 'multiply':
          return a * b;
        case 'divide':
          return a / b;
      }
    },
  },
};

// Infer the types from the tool set
type MyUITools = InferUITools<typeof tools>;
// This creates a type with:
// {
//   weather: { input: { location: string }; output: string };
//   calculator: { input: { operation: 'add' | 'subtract' | 'multiply' | 'divide'; a: number; b: number }; output: number };
// }
```

### Display Tool Invocations in Chat UI - TypeScript React

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Updates the chat UI component to render different message part types, including text and tool invocations. Uses a switch statement to handle tool-weather parts by displaying JSON representation of tool calls and results alongside regular text messages.

```typescript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { useState } from 'react';

export default function Chat() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col w-full max-w-md py-24 mx-auto stretch">
      {messages.map(message => (
        <div key={message.id} className="whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
          {message.parts.map((part, i) => {
            switch (part.type) {
              case 'text':
                return <div key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</div>;
              case 'tool-weather':
                return (
                  <pre key={`${message.id}-${i}`}>
                    {JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}
                  </pre>
                );
            }
          })}
        </div>
      ))}

      <form
        onSubmit={e => {
          e.preventDefault();
          sendMessage({ text: input });
          setInput('');
        }}
      >
        <input
          className="fixed dark:bg-zinc-900 bottom-0 w-full max-w-md p-2 mb-8 border border-zinc-300 dark:border-zinc-800 rounded shadow-xl"
          value={input}
          placeholder="Say something..."
          onChange={e => setInput(e.currentTarget.value)}
        />
      </form>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### Enable Anthropic Reasoning with AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/anthropic

This example illustrates how to enable the reasoning feature for Anthropic models by configuring the `thinking` option in `providerOptions`. By specifying a `budgetTokens`, the model can provide `reasoningText` and detailed `reasoning` alongside the main text response, offering insights into its thought process.

```ts
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, reasoningText, reasoning } = await generateText({
  model: anthropic('claude-opus-4-20250514'),
  prompt: 'How many people will live in the world in 2040?',
  providerOptions: {
    anthropic: {
      thinking: { type: 'enabled', budgetTokens: 12000 },
    } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
  },
});

console.log(reasoningText); // reasoning text
console.log(reasoning); // reasoning details including redacted reasoning
console.log(text); // text response
```

### Provider-Specific Options Configuration

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/configuring-call-options

Shows how to configure provider-specific settings dynamically through call options. The example demonstrates setting OpenAI's reasoning effort based on task difficulty, allowing fine-grained control over model behavior.

```typescript
import { openai, OpenAILanguageModelResponsesOptions } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: 'openai/o3',
  callOptionsSchema: z.object({
    taskDifficulty: z.enum(['low', 'medium', 'high']),
  }),
  prepareCall: ({ options, ...settings }) => ({
    ...settings,
    providerOptions: {
      openai: {
        reasoningEffort: options.taskDifficulty,
      } satisfies OpenAILanguageModelResponsesOptions,
    },
  }),
});

await agent.generate({
  prompt: 'Analyze this complex scenario...',
  options: { taskDifficulty: 'high' },
});
```

### Implement a Custom AI Agent with `Agent` Interface in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/agent

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to create a custom AI agent by implementing the `Agent` interface. It shows how to define `generate` and `stream` methods to process user prompts or messages, returning either a direct text result or a text stream. The example uses `prompt` or `messages` as input and defines an empty `tools` object for compatibility.

```ts
import { Agent, GenerateTextResult, StreamTextResult } from 'ai';
import type { ModelMessage } from '@ai-sdk/provider-utils';

class MyEchoAgent implements Agent {
  version = 'agent-v1' as const;
  id = 'echo';
  tools = {};

  async generate({ prompt, messages, abortSignal }) {
    const text = prompt ?? JSON.stringify(messages);
    return { text, steps: [] };
  }

  async stream({ prompt, messages, abortSignal }) {
    const text = prompt ?? JSON.stringify(messages);
    return {
      textStream: (async function* () {
        yield text;
      })(),
    };
  }
}
```

### Define AI SDK Provider Interfaces and Settings in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/openai-compatible-providers/custom-providers

This TypeScript code defines the `ExampleProviderSettings` interface for configuring the AI SDK provider, including API key, base URL, headers, and a custom fetch function. It also defines the `ExampleProvider` interface, which outlines the methods for creating various AI models like chat, completion, embedding, and image models, ensuring type safety and consistency across the provider.

```ts
import { LanguageModelV1, EmbeddingModelV3 } from '@ai-sdk/provider';
import {
  OpenAICompatibleChatLanguageModel,
  OpenAICompatibleCompletionLanguageModel,
  OpenAICompatibleEmbeddingModel,
  OpenAICompatibleImageModel,
} from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';
import {
  FetchFunction,
  loadApiKey,
  withoutTrailingSlash,
} from '@ai-sdk/provider-utils';
// Import your model id and settings here.

export interface ExampleProviderSettings {
  /**
Example API key.
*/
  apiKey?: string;
  /**
Base URL for the API calls.
*/
  baseURL?: string;
  /**
Custom headers to include in the requests.
*/
  headers?: Record<string, string>;
  /**
Optional custom url query parameters to include in request urls.
*/
  queryParams?: Record<string, string>;
  /**
Custom fetch implementation. You can use it as a middleware to intercept requests,
or to provide a custom fetch implementation for e.g. testing.
*/
  fetch?: FetchFunction;
}

export interface ExampleProvider {
  /**
Creates a model for text generation.
*/
  (
    modelId: ExampleChatModelId,
    settings?: ExampleChatSettings,
  ): LanguageModelV1;

  /**
Creates a chat model for text generation.
*/
  chatModel(
    modelId: ExampleChatModelId,
    settings?: ExampleChatSettings,
  ): LanguageModelV1;

  /**
Creates a completion model for text generation.
*/
  completionModel(
    modelId: ExampleCompletionModelId,
    settings?: ExampleCompletionSettings,
  ): LanguageModelV1;

  /**
Creates a text embedding model for text generation.
*/
  embeddingModel(
    modelId: ExampleEmbeddingModelId,
    settings?: ExampleEmbeddingSettings,
  ): EmbeddingModelV3<string>;

  /**
Creates an image model for image generation.
*/
  imageModel(
    modelId: ExampleImageModelId,
    settings?: ExampleImageSettings,
  ): ImageModelV3;
}
```
