### Implement Sequential AI Generations with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/advanced/sequential-generations

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to perform sequential AI generations using the AI SDK. It first generates blog post ideas, then selects the best idea, and finally creates a detailed outline, with each `generateText` call using the output from the previous step as its prompt input. This pattern is useful for building multi-step AI workflows.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

async function sequentialActions() {
  // Generate blog post ideas
  const ideasGeneration = await generateText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    prompt: 'Generate 10 ideas for a blog post about making spaghetti.',
  });

  console.log('Generated Ideas:\n', ideasGeneration);

  // Pick the best idea
  const bestIdeaGeneration = await generateText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    prompt: `Here are some blog post ideas about making spaghetti:
${ideasGeneration}

Pick the best idea from the list above and explain why it's the best.`,
  });

  console.log('\nBest Idea:\n', bestIdeaGeneration);

  // Generate an outline
  const outlineGeneration = await generateText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    prompt: `We've chosen the following blog post idea about making spaghetti:
${bestIdeaGeneration}

Create a detailed outline for a blog post based on this idea.`,
  });

  console.log('\nBlog Post Outline:\n', outlineGeneration);
}

sequentialActions().catch(console.error);
```

### Example of streaming agent output with `createAgentUIStream` in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/create-agent-ui-stream

This complete example demonstrates how to call `createAgentUIStream` with a concrete user message and an `AbortController` for cancellation. It shows how to await the stream and then iterate through each `UIMessageChunk`, logging it to the console. This pattern is useful for integrating agent output into client-side UIs or logging systems.

```typescript
import { createAgentUIStream } from 'ai';

const controller = new AbortController();

const stream = await createAgentUIStream({
  agent,
  uiMessages: [{ role: 'user', content: 'What is the weather in SF today?' }],
  abortSignal: controller.signal,
  sendStart: true,
  // ...other UIMessageStreamOptions
});

for await (const chunk of stream) {
  // Each chunk is a UI message update — stream it to your client, dashboard, logs, etc.
  console.log(chunk);
}

// Call controller.abort() to cancel the agent operation early.
```

### Access Step Information in ToolLoopAgent Callbacks

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/loop-control

Shows how to access detailed execution information in prepareStep and stopWhen callbacks, including model configuration, step number, previous steps with results, and messages. The example demonstrates accessing previous tool calls and making decisions based on execution history.

```typescript
prepareStep: async ({
  model, // Current model configuration
  stepNumber, // Current step number (0-indexed)
  steps, // All previous steps with their results
  messages, // Messages to be sent to the model
}) => {
  // Access previous tool calls and results
  const previousToolCalls = steps.flatMap(step => step.toolCalls);
  const previousResults = steps.flatMap(step => step.toolResults);

  // Make decisions based on execution history
  if (previousToolCalls.some(call => call.toolName === 'dataAnalysis')) {
    return {
      toolChoice: { type: 'tool', toolName: 'reportGenerator' },
    };
  }

  return {};
},
```

### Implement Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG) with ToolLoopAgent

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/configuring-call-options

Create a RAG agent that fetches relevant documents and injects them as context into the prompt. The prepareCall function supports async operations, allowing you to perform vector searches or database queries before configuring the agent. This enables context-aware responses based on retrieved documents.

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

const ragAgent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  callOptionsSchema: z.object({
    query: z.string(),
  }),
  prepareCall: async ({ options, ...settings }) => {
    // Fetch relevant documents (this can be async)
    const documents = await vectorSearch(options.query);

    return {
      ...settings,
      instructions: `Answer questions using the following context:

${documents.map(doc => doc.content).join('\n\n')}`,
    };
  },
});

await ragAgent.generate({
  prompt: 'What is our refund policy?',
  options: { query: 'refund policy' },
});
```

## listResources

### Description

### Method

### Parameters

- **options** (object) - Optional - Configuration options for listing resources.
  - **params** (PaginatedRequest['params']) - Optional - Optional pagination parameters including cursor.

### Define Weather Tool in Chat Route Handler - TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Creates a weather tool for the AI model with Zod schema validation and async execution. The tool accepts a location string parameter and returns simulated weather data. This enables the model to generate tool calls when users ask about weather conditions.

```typescript
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages, tool } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Configure Agent with Tools and Context (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/agent-skills

This section defines the `callOptionsSchema` for passing `Sandbox` and skill metadata to the agent. It then creates `readFileTool` and `bashTool` for basic file system and command execution. Finally, it initializes a `ToolLoopAgent`, wiring up `loadSkill`, `readFile`, and `bash` tools, and configures `prepareCall` to dynamically inject skill descriptions into the agent's instructions and provide `sandbox` and `skills` in the experimental context.

```ts
const callOptionsSchema = z.object({
  sandbox: z.custom<Sandbox>(),
  skills: z.array(
    z.object({
      name: z.string(),
      description: z.string(),
      path: z.string(),
    }),
  ),
});

const readFileTool = tool({
  description: 'Read a file from the filesystem',
  inputSchema: z.object({ path: z.string() }),
  execute: async ({ path }, { experimental_context }) => {
    const { sandbox } = experimental_context as { sandbox: Sandbox };
    return sandbox.readFile(path, 'utf-8');
  },
});

const bashTool = tool({
  description: 'Execute a bash command',
  inputSchema: z.object({ command: z.string() }),
  execute: async ({ command }, { experimental_context }) => {
    const { sandbox } = experimental_context as { sandbox: Sandbox };
    return sandbox.exec(command);
  },
});

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: yourModel,
  tools: {
    loadSkill: loadSkillTool,
    readFile: readFileTool,
    bash: bashTool,
  },
  callOptionsSchema,
  prepareCall: ({ options, ...settings }) => ({
    ...settings,
    instructions: `${settings.instructions}\n\n${buildSkillsPrompt(options.skills)}`,
    experimental_context: {
      sandbox: options.sandbox,
      skills: options.skills,
    },
  }),
});
```

### Function: createProviderRegistry

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/provider-registry

Details on how to use and configure the `createProviderRegistry` function, including its parameters and usage examples for different model types.

```APIDOC
## Function: createProviderRegistry()

### Description
The `createProviderRegistry()` function allows you to manage multiple AI providers and their models from a central location. It enables accessing models through simple string IDs, typically in the format `providerId:modelId`.

### Method
Function

### Endpoint
`createProviderRegistry()`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
(None)

#### Query Parameters
(None)

#### Request Body
- **`providers`** `Record<string, Provider>` - Required - An object where keys are unique provider identifiers (strings) and values are `Provider` objects. Each `Provider` object defines how to access its specific model types.
  - **`Provider` type properties**:
    - **`languageModel`** `(id: string) => LanguageModel` - A function that takes a model ID string and returns a `LanguageModel` instance for that provider.
    - **`embeddingModel`** `(id: string) => EmbeddingModel<string>` - A function that takes a model ID string and returns an `EmbeddingModel` instance for that provider.
    - **`imageModel`** `(id: string) => ImageModel` - A function that takes a model ID string and returns an `ImageModel` instance for that provider.
- **`options`** `object` - Optional - An optional configuration object for the registry.
  - **`Options` type properties**:
    - **`separator`** `string` - Optional - A custom string to use as the separator between the provider ID and the model ID. Defaults to `":"`.
    - **`languageModelMiddleware`** `LanguageModelMiddleware | LanguageModelMiddleware[]` - Optional - Middleware or an array of middleware functions to apply to all language models obtained from this registry.
    - **`imageModelMiddleware`** `ImageModelMiddleware | ImageModelMiddleware[]` - Optional - Middleware or an array of middleware functions to apply to all image models obtained from this registry.

### Request Example
```typescript
import { anthropic } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { createProviderRegistry } from 'ai';

export const registry = createProviderRegistry({
  anthropic,
  openai: createOpenAI({
    apiKey: process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY,
  }),
}, { separator: ' > ' }); // Example with custom separator
```

### Response
#### Success Response (Registry Object)
The function returns a `Registry` object. This object provides methods to retrieve specific model instances.
- **`languageModel`** `(id: string) => LanguageModel` - Method to access language models.
- **`embeddingModel`** `(id: string) => EmbeddingModel<string>` - Method to access text embedding models.
- **`imageModel`** `(id: string) => ImageModel` - Method to access image models.

#### Response Example
```typescript
// Example of using the returned registry object
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { registry } from './registry'; // Assuming registry is the returned object

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: registry.languageModel('openai:gpt-4.1'),
  prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
});

console.log(text);
```
```

### Implement AI SDK Tool Input Lifecycle Hooks (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/tools-and-tool-calling

This example illustrates the use of tool input lifecycle hooks (`onInputStart`, `onInputDelta`, `onInputAvailable`) within an AI SDK `streamText` call. These hooks provide visibility into the tool's input generation process, allowing developers to log or react to the input as it's being streamed or when it becomes fully available. `onInputStart` and `onInputDelta` are specific to streaming contexts.

```ts
import { streamText, tool } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

const result = streamText({
  model: __MODEL__,
  tools: {
    getWeather: tool({
      description: 'Get the weather in a location',
      inputSchema: z.object({
        location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for')
      }),
      execute: async ({ location }) => ({
        temperature: 72 + Math.floor(Math.random() * 21) - 10
      }),
      onInputStart: () => {
        console.log('Tool call starting');
      },
      onInputDelta: ({ inputTextDelta }) => {
        console.log('Received input chunk:', inputTextDelta);
      },
      onInputAvailable: ({ input }) => {
        console.log('Complete input:', input);
      }
    })
  },
  prompt: 'What is the weather in San Francisco?'
});
```

### Implement Chat UI with AI SDK's useChat Hook in React Native

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

This code sets up a chat interface in a React Native application using the AI SDK's `useChat` hook. It displays a list of messages, handles user input, and sends messages to an API route using `sendMessage`. The `expo/fetch` library is used for streaming responses, requiring Expo 52+.

```tsx
import { generateAPIUrl } from '@/utils';
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';
import { DefaultChatTransport } from 'ai';
import { fetch as expoFetch } from 'expo/fetch';
import { useState } from 'react';
import { View, TextInput, ScrollView, Text, SafeAreaView } from 'react-native';

export default function App() {
  const [input, setInput] = useState('');
  const { messages, error, sendMessage } = useChat({
    transport: new DefaultChatTransport({
      fetch: expoFetch as unknown as typeof globalThis.fetch,
      api: generateAPIUrl('/api/chat'),
    }),
    onError: error => console.error(error, 'ERROR'),
  });

  if (error) return <Text>{error.message}</Text>;

  return (
    <SafeAreaView style={{ height: '100%' }}>
      <View
        style={{
          height: '95%',
          display: 'flex',
          flexDirection: 'column',
          paddingHorizontal: 8,
        }}
      >
        <ScrollView style={{ flex: 1 }}>
          {messages.map(m => (
            <View key={m.id} style={{ marginVertical: 8 }}>
              <View>
                <Text style={{ fontWeight: 700 }}>{m.role}</Text>
                {m.parts.map((part, i) => {
                  switch (part.type) {
                    case 'text':
                      return <Text key={`${m.id}-${i}`}>{part.text}</Text>;
                  }
                })}
              </View>
            </View>
          ))}
        </ScrollView>

        <View style={{ marginTop: 8 }}>
          <TextInput
            style={{ backgroundColor: 'white', padding: 8 }}
            placeholder="Say something..."
            value={input}
            onChange={e => setInput(e.nativeEvent.text)}
            onSubmitEditing={e => {
              e.preventDefault();
              sendMessage({ text: input });
              setInput('');
            }}
            autoFocus={true}
          />
        </View>
      </View>
    </SafeAreaView>
  );
}
```

--------------------------------

### Initialize Memory Filesystem with Bootstrap Defaults

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/custom-memory-tool

Sets up the memory directory structure (.memory) and creates default files for core memory, notes, and conversations. Uses Node.js filesystem promises API to check file existence and write defaults only if files don't already exist. This ensures a consistent memory structure on startup.

```typescript
import {
  access,
  appendFile,
  mkdir,
  readFile,
  writeFile,
} from 'node:fs/promises';
import { join, resolve } from 'node:path';

const MEMORY_DIR = '.memory';
const MEMORY_ROOT = resolve(process.cwd(), MEMORY_DIR);
const CORE_MEMORY_PATH = join(MEMORY_ROOT, 'core.md');
const NOTES_PATH = join(MEMORY_ROOT, 'notes.md');
const CONVERSATIONS_PATH = join(MEMORY_ROOT, 'conversations.jsonl');

const DEFAULT_CORE_MEMORY = `# Core Memory
- Keep this short.
- Put stable user facts here.
`;

const DEFAULT_NOTES = `# Notes
Use this file for detailed memories and timestamped notes.
`;

async function ensureFile(path: string, content: string): Promise<void> {
  try {
    await access(path);
  } catch {
    await writeFile(path, content, 'utf8');
  }
}

async function ensureMemoryFilesystem(): Promise<void> {
  await mkdir(MEMORY_ROOT, { recursive: true });
  await ensureFile(CORE_MEMORY_PATH, DEFAULT_CORE_MEMORY);
  await ensureFile(NOTES_PATH, DEFAULT_NOTES);
  await ensureFile(CONVERSATIONS_PATH, '');
}
```

### Setup OpenTelemetry Node SDK for Non-NextJS Applications

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/observability/mlflow

Manual configuration of OpenTelemetry Node SDK with OTLP exporter for Node.js applications. Initializes tracing, makes AI SDK call with telemetry, and shuts down SDK.

```typescript
import { init } from 'mlflow-tracing';
import { generateText } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { NodeSDK } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-node';
import { SimpleSpanProcessor } from '@opentelemetry/sdk-trace-node';
import { OTLPTraceExporter } from '@opentelemetry/exporter-trace-otlp-proto';

const sdk = new NodeSDK({
  spanProcessors: [
    new SimpleSpanProcessor(
      new OTLPTraceExporter({
        url: '<your-mlflow-tracking-server-endpoint>/v1/traces',
        headers: { 'x-mlflow-experiment-id': '<your-experiment-id>' },
      }),
    ),
  ],
});

sdk.start();
init();

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'What is MLflow?',
  experimental_telemetry: { isEnabled: true },
});

console.log(result.text);
sdk.shutdown();
```

### Define Assistant Message with File Content in AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/foundations/prompts

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: __MODEL__,
  messages: [
    { role: 'user', content: 'Generate an image of a roquefort cheese!' },
    {
      role: 'assistant',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'file',
          mediaType: 'image/png',
          data: fs.readFileSync('./data/roquefort.jpg'),
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Configure Provider-Specific Settings for AI SDK experimental_generateVideo (TypeScript/TSX)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/video-generation

This example illustrates how to pass provider-specific settings to the `experimental_generateVideo` function using the `providerOptions` parameter. These options, such as `loop` and `motionStrength` for the Fal provider, become request body properties, allowing fine-grained control over the video generation process.

```tsx
import { experimental_generateVideo as generateVideo } from 'ai';
import { fal } from '@ai-sdk/fal';

const { video } = await generateVideo({
  model: fal.video('luma-dream-machine/ray-2'),
  prompt: 'A cat walking on a treadmill',
  aspectRatio: '16:9',
  providerOptions: {
    fal: { loop: true, motionStrength: 0.8 }
  }
});
```

### GET /resource-templates

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/mcp-tools

Lists all available resource templates from the MCP server. Resource templates are dynamic URI patterns that allow flexible queries for accessing resources.

```APIDOC
## GET /resource-templates

### Description
Lists all available resource templates that define dynamic URI patterns for flexible resource queries.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/resource-templates

### Request Example
```typescript
const templates = await mcpClient.listResourceTemplates();
```

### Response
- **templates** (array) - Collection of available resource template patterns
  - Each template includes URI pattern and parameters

### Resource Templates
- Dynamic URI patterns for flexible queries
- Allow parameterized resource access
- Enable pattern-based resource discovery

### Notes
- Templates define how to construct resource URIs
- Use templates to generate specific resource URIs
- Enables dynamic resource access patterns
- Per MCP specification for resource management
```

### Simulate UI Message Stream Responses in Next.js

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/testing

Demonstrates simulating UI Message Stream responses for testing, debugging, or demonstration purposes in a Next.js API route. The example shows how to configure initial and chunk delays, structure event stream data, and set appropriate HTTP headers for Server-Sent Events (SSE) communication.

```TypeScript
import { simulateReadableStream } from 'ai';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  return new Response(
    simulateReadableStream({
      initialDelayInMs: 1000,
      chunkDelayInMs: 300,
      chunks: [
        `data: {"type":"start","messageId":"msg-123"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-start","id":"text-1"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":"This"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":" is an"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-delta","id":"text-1","delta":" example."}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"text-end","id":"text-1"}\n\n`,
        `data: {"type":"finish"}\n\n`,
        `data: [DONE]\n\n`,
      ],
    }).pipeThrough(new TextEncoderStream()),
    {
      status: 200,
      headers: {
        'Content-Type': 'text/event-stream',
        'Cache-Control': 'no-cache',
        Connection: 'keep-alive',
        'x-vercel-ai-ui-message-stream': 'v1',
      },
    },
  );
}
```

### Extend API Route with Multiple Tools for Weather and Temperature Conversion

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

Enhance the API route by adding a second tool for converting Fahrenheit to Celsius. The weather tool retrieves temperature data, and the convertFahrenheitToCelsius tool processes the temperature value. Both tools work within the 5-step limit defined by stopWhen condition.

```typescript
import {
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
      convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
        description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          temperature: z
            .number()
            .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
          const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
          return {
            celsius,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none',
    },
  });
}
```

### GET /resources

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/mcp-tools

Lists all available resources from the MCP server. Resources are application-driven data sources that provide context to the model, controlled by the application rather than the model.

```APIDOC
## GET /resources

### Description
Lists all available resources from the MCP server that can be used to provide context to the model.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/resources

### Request Example
```typescript
const resources = await mcpClient.listResources();
```

### Response
- **resources** (array) - Collection of available resources
  - Each resource includes URI and metadata

### Resource Characteristics
- Application-driven data sources
- Provide context to the model
- Application controls when resources are fetched and passed
- Unlike tools, resources are not model-controlled

### Notes
- Use this to discover available resources before reading them
- Resources are passive context providers
- Per MCP specification for resource management
```

### Implement Custom File Download Function for AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/foundations/prompts

This example shows how to provide a custom `experimental_download` function to the `generateText` API. This function allows for advanced control over file downloads, enabling features like throttling, retries, authentication, or caching for files referenced by URLs in the messages. The custom function receives an array of `requestedDownloads` and should return an array of `Uint8Array` data or `null`.

```ts
const result = await generateText({
  model: __MODEL__,
  experimental_download: async (
    requestedDownloads: Array<{
      url: URL;
      isUrlSupportedByModel: boolean;
    }>,
  ): PromiseLike<
    Array<{
      data: Uint8Array;
      mediaType: string | undefined;
    } | null>
  > => {
    // ... download the files and return an array with similar order
  },
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'file',
          data: new URL('https://api.company.com/private/document.pdf'),
          mediaType: 'application/pdf',
        },
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### prepareStep Callback Configuration with Model and Tool Options

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/tools-and-tool-calling

Demonstrates using the prepareStep callback to customize step execution by changing the model, setting tool choices, and limiting available tools. The callback receives model, stepNumber, steps, and messages parameters and returns configuration overrides for the current step.

```typescript
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  // ...
  prepareStep: async ({ model, stepNumber, steps, messages }) => {
    if (stepNumber === 0) {
      return {
        // use a different model for this step:
        model: modelForThisParticularStep,
        // force a tool choice for this step:
        toolChoice: { type: 'tool', toolName: 'tool1' },
        // limit the tools that are available for this step:
        activeTools: ['tool1'],
      };
    }

    // when nothing is returned, the default settings are used
  },
});
```

### Configure Client Sampling with Model Preferences using TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/mcp-sampling

This TypeScript code demonstrates how to set up client-side sampling for an MCP client that lacks native support. It initializes an MCP client, configures `setupClientSampling` to handle AI model requests using `selectModelFromPreferences` for dynamic model selection based on hints and priorities, and integrates with the AI SDK's `generateText` function. The example also shows how to connect the client to a `StdioClientTransport`.

```typescript
import { Client } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/index.js';
import { StdioClientTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/client/stdio.js';
import {
  convertAISDKFinishReasonToMCP,
  selectModelFromPreferences,
  setupClientSampling,
} from '@mcpc-tech/mcp-sampling-ai-provider';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const client = new Client(
  { name: 'my-client', version: '1.0.0' },
  { capabilities: { sampling: {} } },
);

setupClientSampling(client, {
  handler: async params => {
    const modelId = selectModelFromPreferences(params.modelPreferences, {
      hints: {
        'gpt-5': 'openai/gpt-5-mini',
        'gpt-mini': 'openai/gpt-5-mini',
      },
      priorities: {
        speed: 'openai/gpt-5-mini',
        intelligence: 'openai/gpt-5-mini',
      },
      default: 'openai/gpt-5-mini',
    });

    const result = await generateText({
      model: modelId,
      messages: params.messages,
    });

    return {
      model: modelId,
      role: 'assistant',
      content: { type: 'text', text: result.text },
      stopReason: convertAISDKFinishReasonToMCP(result.finishReason),
    };
  },
});

const transport = new StdioClientTransport({
  command: 'npx',
  args: ['-y', 'example_mcp_server.ts'],
});

await client.connect(transport);
```

### Integrate Letta Cloud as AI SDK Model

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/memory

This TypeScript example shows how to configure an AI SDK agent to use Letta Cloud as its model. By setting the `model` to `lettaCloud()` and providing the agent ID in `providerOptions`, the agent transparently handles memory management through Letta's platform. This approach simplifies memory integration as storage, retrieval, and injection are managed externally.

```ts
import { lettaCloud } from '@letta-ai/vercel-ai-sdk-provider';
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: lettaCloud(),
  providerOptions: {
    letta: {
      agent: { id: 'your-agent-id' },
    },
  },
});

const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: 'Remember that my favorite editor is Neovim',
});
```

### Create an API route for streaming chat responses in Expo

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

Defines an asynchronous POST request handler at `app/api/chat+api.ts` for streaming chat responses. It extracts user messages, uses `streamText` from the AI SDK to generate a response, and converts it into a UI message stream for the client.

```tsx
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none'
    }
  });
}
```

### Generate Image-to-Video with Alibaba AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/alibaba

This snippet demonstrates generating a video from an initial image and an optional text prompt using the Alibaba AI SDK. It uses `alibaba.video('wan2.6-i2v')` and provides an image URL and text for the prompt. The `pollTimeoutMs` option is set to manage the asynchronous video generation process.

```ts
import { alibaba, type AlibabaVideoModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/alibaba';

### Start Step Stream Part

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/stream-text

Marks the beginning of a new step in the stream. Contains metadata about the request sent to the language model provider, including the raw HTTP body and any warnings.

```APIDOC
## TextStreamPart - Start Step

### Description
Indicates the start of a new step in the stream with associated request metadata.

### Parameters
- **type** (string) - Required - Value: 'start-step' - Identifies the start of a new step
- **request** (LanguageModelRequestMetadata) - Required - Information about the request sent to the language model provider
  - **body** (string) - Raw request HTTP body sent to the provider API as a string
- **warnings** (Warning[]) - Optional - Warnings from the model provider (e.g., unsupported settings)

### Response Example
```json
{
  "type": "start-step",
  "request": {
    "body": "{\"model\": \"gpt-4\", \"messages\": [...], \"tools\": [...]}"
  },
  "warnings": []
}
```
```

### Transcribe Audio with OpenAI and AI SDK, Specifying Language (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/openai

This example shows how to transcribe audio using the `experimental_transcribe` function from AI SDK, passing an OpenAI transcription model. It includes `providerOptions` to specify the input language (e.g., 'en'), which can improve accuracy and latency. The `audio` input is a `Uint8Array`.

```ts
import { experimental_transcribe as transcribe } from 'ai';
import { openai, type OpenAITranscriptionModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const result = await transcribe({
  model: openai.transcription('whisper-1'),
  audio: new Uint8Array([1, 2, 3, 4]),
  providerOptions: {
    openai: { language: 'en' } satisfies OpenAITranscriptionModelOptions,
  },
});
```

### Generate Images with Imagen

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-vertex

Generate images using the Imagen model on Vertex AI. This basic example demonstrates how to create an image from a text prompt with aspect ratio configuration.

```APIDOC
## generateImage - Imagen Model

### Description
Generate images using the Imagen model on Google Vertex AI with text prompts and aspect ratio configuration.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
Vertex AI Imagen API

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **model** (string) - Required - The Imagen model identifier (e.g., 'imagen-4.0-generate-001')
- **prompt** (string) - Required - Text description of the image to generate
- **aspectRatio** (string) - Optional - Aspect ratio for the generated image (e.g., '16:9')

### Request Example
```ts
import { vertex } from '@ai-sdk/google-vertex';
import { generateImage } from 'ai';

const { image } = await generateImage({
  model: vertex.image('imagen-4.0-generate-001'),
  prompt: 'A futuristic cityscape at sunset',
  aspectRatio: '16:9',
});
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **image** (string) - The generated image data

### Notes
- Imagen models do not support the `size` parameter; use `aspectRatio` instead
- The `imagen-4.0-generate-001` model does not support image editing operations
```

### Example `pruneMessages` Usage with Reasoning and Tool Call Options (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-ui/prune-messages

This example illustrates a direct call to `pruneMessages` with common configuration options. It demonstrates how to remove all reasoning parts and prune tool calls from all messages except the last one, providing a clear pattern for context optimization.

```typescript
import { pruneMessages } from 'ai';

const pruned = pruneMessages({
  messages,
  reasoning: 'all', // Remove all reasoning parts
  toolCalls: 'before-last-message', // Remove tool calls except those in the last message
});
```

### Integrate Letta Memory Tools with AI SDK Agent

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/memory

This TypeScript example illustrates how to use specific Letta memory tools, such as `core_memory_append`, `memory_insert`, and `memory_replace`, alongside an AI SDK agent. It demonstrates how to explicitly define these tools within the agent's configuration, allowing for fine-grained control over memory operations while still leveraging Letta's backend. This enables combining Letta's built-in memory capabilities with custom agent logic.

```ts
import { lettaCloud } from '@letta-ai/vercel-ai-sdk-provider';
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: lettaCloud(),
  tools: {
    core_memory_append: lettaCloud.tool('core_memory_append'),
    memory_insert: lettaCloud.tool('memory_insert'),
    memory_replace: lettaCloud.tool('memory_replace'),
  },
  providerOptions: {
    letta: {
      agent: { id: 'your-agent-id' },
    },
  },
});

const stream = agent.stream({
  prompt: 'What do you remember about me?',
});
```

### Initialize Computer Tool for Keyboard/Mouse Control with Vertex Anthropic AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-vertex

This snippet shows how to initialize the `computer_20241022` tool from the Vertex Anthropic AI SDK, enabling programmatic control over keyboard and mouse actions. It requires `displayWidthPx`, `displayHeightPx`, and optionally `displayNumber` for configuration. The `execute` function handles different actions like `screenshot`, `key`, `type`, `mouse_move`, and `click` events, returning results which can be mapped to model output via `toModelOutput` for LLM consumption.

```ts
const computerTool = vertexAnthropic.tools.computer_20241022({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0, // Optional, for X11 environments

  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    // Implement your computer control logic here
    // Return the result of the action

    // Example code:
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        // multipart result:
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs
            .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
            .toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },

  // map to tool result content for LLM consumption:
  toModelOutput({ output }) {
    return typeof output === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: output }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: output.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Set up Chat UI with Svelte and AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/svelte

Initialize a Svelte component that uses the AI SDK's Chat class to display chat messages and handle user input. The Chat class manages state for messages and provides sendMessage function to communicate with the backend API route. Messages are displayed with their role and text parts, and a form handles user submissions.

```svelte
<script lang="ts">
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';

  let input = '';
  const chat = new Chat({});

  function handleSubmit(event: SubmitEvent) {
    event.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input });
    input = '';
  }
</script>

<main>
  <ul>
    {#each chat.messages as message, messageIndex (messageIndex)}
      <li>
        <div>{message.role}</div>
        <div>
          {#each message.parts as part, partIndex (partIndex)}
            {#if part.type === 'text'}
              <div>{part.text}</div>
            {/if}
          {/each}
        </div>
      </li>
    {/each}
  </ul>
  <form onsubmit={handleSubmit}>
    <input bind:value={input} />
    <button type="submit">Send</button>
  </form>
</main>
```

### Configure provider-specific reranking options in AI SDK

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/reranking

This example demonstrates how to pass provider-specific configuration options to the reranking model using the `providerOptions` parameter. It shows how to set parameters like `maxTokensPerDoc` for a Cohere model, allowing fine-grained control over the reranking process.

```ts
import { cohere } from '@ai-sdk/cohere';
import { rerank } from 'ai';

const { ranking } = await rerank({
  model: cohere.reranking('rerank-v3.5'),
  documents: ['sunny day at the beach', 'rainy afternoon in the city'],
  query: 'talk about rain',
  providerOptions: {
    cohere: {
      maxTokensPerDoc: 1000,
    },
  },
});
```

### Example usage of `pipeUIMessageStreamToResponse` in TypeScript/TSX

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-ui/pipe-ui-message-stream-to-response

This example demonstrates how to use `pipeUIMessageStreamToResponse` to send a UI message stream to a Node.js `ServerResponse`. It configures the response status, status text, custom headers, and provides an optional callback to consume the underlying SSE stream independently. This is useful for streaming UI updates from a server.

```tsx
pipeUIMessageStreamToResponse({
  response: serverResponse,
  status: 200,
  statusText: 'OK',
  headers: {
    'Custom-Header': 'value',
  },
  stream: myUIMessageStream,
  consumeSseStream: ({ stream }) => {
    // Optional: consume the SSE stream independently
    console.log('Consuming SSE stream:', stream);
  },
});
```

### Add a Fahrenheit to Celsius Conversion Tool to AI Gateway API Route (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nuxt

This snippet extends the existing `server/api/chat.ts` file by adding a new tool, `convertFahrenheitToCelsius`, to the AI model's capabilities. This tool takes a temperature in Fahrenheit as input and returns its Celsius equivalent, demonstrating how to integrate multiple tools for more sophisticated multi-step interactions. It leverages the `ai` SDK's `tool` function and `zod` for input schema definition.

```typescript
import {
  createGateway,
  streamText,
  UIMessage,
  convertToModelMessages,
  tool,
  stepCountIs,
} from 'ai';
import { z } from 'zod';

export default defineLazyEventHandler(async () => {
  const apiKey = useRuntimeConfig().aiGatewayApiKey;
  if (!apiKey) throw new Error('Missing AI Gateway API key');
  const gateway = createGateway({
    apiKey: apiKey,
  });

  return defineEventHandler(async (event: any) => {
    const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await readBody(event);

    const result = streamText({
      model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
      messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return {
              location,
              temperature,
            };
          },
        }),
        convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
          description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            temperature: z
              .number()
              .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
            const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
            return {
              celsius,
            };
          },
        }),
      },
    });

    return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
  });
});
```

import type { GatewayLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/gateway';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: 'anthropic/claude-sonnet-4',
  prompt: 'Write a haiku about programming',

### Prepare Request Body with experimental_prepareRequestBody in AI SDK v4

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/migration-guides/migration-guide-5-0

Demonstrates the v4 approach to customizing the request body sent to the server using the experimental_prepareRequestBody option. This example shows how to send only the last message.

```typescript
import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

const { messages } = useChat({
  api: '/api/chat',
  // Only send the last message to the server:
  experimental_prepareRequestBody({ messages, id }) {
    return { message: messages[messages.length - 1], id };
  },
});
```

### Apply `defaultSettingsMiddleware` to a Wrapped Language Model in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/default-settings-middleware

This example illustrates how to integrate `defaultSettingsMiddleware` with `wrapLanguageModel` to create a model instance with predefined default settings. It demonstrates how these defaults are applied during a `streamText` call and how explicitly provided parameters (e.g., `temperature`) take precedence over the configured defaults.

```ts
import { streamText, wrapLanguageModel, defaultSettingsMiddleware } from 'ai';

// Create a model with default settings
const modelWithDefaults = wrapLanguageModel({
  model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
  middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
    settings: {
      providerOptions: {
        openai: {
          reasoningEffort: 'high',
        },
      },
    },
  }),
});

// Use the model - default settings will be applied
const result = await streamText({
  model: modelWithDefaults,
  prompt: 'Your prompt here',
  // These parameters will override the defaults
  temperature: 0.8,
});
```

### Update Vue.js Component to Display AI SDK Tool Outputs

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nuxt

This Vue.js component (`index.vue`) demonstrates how to integrate with `@ai-sdk/vue` to manage chat messages. It specifically updates the message rendering logic to differentiate and display various `part.type`s, including plain text and structured JSON outputs from `tool-weather` and `tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius` tools, enhancing the UI to show multi-step AI interactions.

```vue
<script setup lang="ts">
import { Chat } from "@ai-sdk/vue";
import { ref } from "vue";

const input = ref("");
const chat = new Chat({});

const handleSubmit = (e: Event) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input.value });
    input.value = "";
};
</script>

<template>
    <div>
        <div v-for="(m, index) in chat.messages" :key="m.id ? m.id : index">
            {{ m.role === "user" ? "User: " : "AI: " }}
            <div
                v-for="(part, index) in m.parts"
                :key="`${m.id}-${part.type}-${index}`"
            >
                <div v-if="part.type === 'text'">{{ part.text }}</div>
                <pre
                    v-if="
                        part.type === 'tool-weather' ||
                        part.type === 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius'
                    "
                    >{{ JSON.stringify(part, null, 2) }}</pre
                >
            </div>
        </div>

        <form @submit="handleSubmit">
            <input v-model="input" placeholder="Say something..." />
        </form>
    </div>
</template>
```

### Configure Google Search Grounding with AI SDK in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-generative-ai

This TypeScript example demonstrates how to integrate Google Search as a grounding tool within the AI SDK using the `@ai-sdk/google` provider. It shows how to import `generateText` and `google`, configure the `google_search` tool, and access detailed `groundingMetadata` and `safetyRatings` from the response's `providerMetadata` for enhanced context and type safety.

```ts
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
  tools: {
    google_search: google.tools.googleSearch({}),
  },
  prompt:
    'List the top 5 San Francisco news from the past week.' +
    'You must include the date of each article.',
});

// access the grounding metadata. Casting to the provider metadata type
// is optional but provides autocomplete and type safety.
const metadata = providerMetadata?.google as
  | GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata
  | undefined;
const groundingMetadata = metadata?.groundingMetadata;
const safetyRatings = metadata?.safetyRatings;
```

### Send PDF File as User Message Part with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/prompts

This example illustrates how to send a PDF file as a message part, specifying its 'mediaType' and providing the file data as a 'Buffer' using 'fs.readFileSync'. It also includes an optional 'filename'. This functionality is supported by specific providers and models for document analysis, such as Google Generative AI.

```typescript
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-1.5-flash'),
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        { type: 'text', text: 'What is the file about?' },
        {
          type: 'file',
          mediaType: 'application/pdf',
          data: fs.readFileSync('./data/example.pdf'),
          filename: 'example.pdf' // optional, not used by all providers
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
});
```

### Track Agent Step Progress with onStepFinish

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/building-agents

Use onStepFinish callback in generate() to track each step's progress including token usage, finish reason, and tool calls. Useful for monitoring and billing purposes.

```typescript
const result = await myAgent.generate({
  prompt: 'Research and summarize the latest AI trends',
  onStepFinish: async ({ usage, finishReason, toolCalls }) => {
    console.log('Step completed:', {
      inputTokens: usage.inputTokens,
      outputTokens: usage.outputTokens,
      finishReason,
      toolsUsed: toolCalls?.map(tc => tc.toolName),
    });
  },
});
```

### Initialize Vertex AI Language Model

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-vertex

Create a language model instance that calls the Google Vertex API. The model ID (e.g., 'gemini-1.5-pro') is passed as the first argument. Custom models must have names starting with 'projects/'.

```APIDOC
## vertex(modelId)

### Description
Initializes a Google Vertex AI language model instance for use with the AI SDK.

### Parameters
- **modelId** (string) - Required - The model identifier (e.g., 'gemini-1.5-pro'). Custom models must start with 'projects/'.

### Request Example
```ts
const model = vertex('gemini-1.5-pro');
```

### Custom Model Example
```ts
const customModel = vertex('projects/my-project/locations/us-central1/models/my-model');
```

### Returns
- A configured language model instance ready for use with generateText() and streamText() functions.
```

### Create advanced provider registry with custom providers and middleware

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/provider-management

Set up a comprehensive provider registry combining multiple providers with namespace prefixes, model aliases, pre-configured settings, and middleware. This example demonstrates gateway pass-through, custom OpenAI-compatible providers, model name aliases, default settings middleware, fallback providers, and limited provider access patterns.

```typescript
import { anthropic, AnthropicLanguageModelOptions } from '@ai-sdk/anthropic';
import { createOpenAICompatible } from '@ai-sdk/openai-compatible';
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';
import {
  createProviderRegistry,
  customProvider,
  defaultSettingsMiddleware,
  gateway,
  wrapLanguageModel,
} from 'ai';

export const registry = createProviderRegistry(
  {
    // pass through gateway with a namespace prefix
    gateway,

    // pass through full providers with namespace prefixes
    xai,

    // access an OpenAI-compatible provider with custom setup
    custom: createOpenAICompatible({
      name: 'provider-name',
      apiKey: process.env.CUSTOM_API_KEY,
      baseURL: 'https://api.custom.com/v1',
    }),

    // setup model name aliases
    anthropic: customProvider({
      languageModels: {
        fast: anthropic('claude-haiku-4-5'),

        // simple model
        writing: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-5'),

        // extended reasoning model configuration:
        reasoning: wrapLanguageModel({
          model: anthropic('claude-sonnet-4-5'),
          middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
            settings: {
              maxOutputTokens: 100000, // example default setting
              providerOptions: {
                anthropic: {
                  thinking: {
                    type: 'enabled',
                    budgetTokens: 32000,
                  },
                } satisfies AnthropicLanguageModelOptions,
              },
            },
          }),
        }),
      },
      fallbackProvider: anthropic,
    }),

    // limit a provider to certain models without a fallback
    groq: customProvider({
      languageModels: {
        'gemma2-9b-it': groq('gemma2-9b-it'),
        'qwen-qwq-32b': groq('qwen-qwq-32b'),
      },
    }),
  },
  { separator: ' > ' },
);

// usage:
const model = registry.languageModel('anthropic > reasoning');
```

--------------------------------

### Initialize Computer Tool for Keyboard and Mouse Control

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/amazon-bedrock

Creates a computer tool instance for controlling keyboard and mouse actions on a computer with specified display dimensions. Supports actions like screenshot, key press, text typing, and mouse movements. Includes a toModelOutput function to map tool results to LLM-consumable content format.

```typescript
const computerTool = bedrock.tools.computer_20241022({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0,

  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs
            .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
            .toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },

  toModelOutput({ output }) {
    return typeof output === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: output }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: output.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Generate Dynamic API URLs for Expo React Native Applications

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

This utility function, `generateAPIUrl`, constructs API endpoint URLs dynamically for Expo React Native projects. It adapts the base URL based on the environment (development or production) and ensures compatibility with `expo/fetch`. In production, it relies on the `EXPO_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL` environment variable for the API server's base URL.

```ts
import Constants from 'expo-constants';

export const generateAPIUrl = (relativePath: string) => {
  const origin = Constants.experienceUrl.replace('exp://', 'http://');

  const path = relativePath.startsWith('/') ? relativePath : `/${relativePath}`;

  if (process.env.NODE_ENV === 'development') {
    return origin.concat(path);
  }

  if (!process.env.EXPO_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL) {
    throw new Error(
      'EXPO_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL environment variable is not defined',
    );
  }

  return process.env.EXPO_PUBLIC_API_BASE_URL.concat(path);
};
```

### GET /tools - Schema Discovery

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/mcp-tools

Retrieves all available tools from the MCP server with automatic schema inference. This approach provides simplicity and automatic synchronization with server changes but without TypeScript type safety.

```APIDOC
## GET /tools (Schema Discovery)

### Description
Automatically discovers and lists all tools offered by the MCP server with inferred input parameter types based on server-provided schemas.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/tools

### Request Example
```typescript
const tools = await mcpClient.tools();
```

### Response
- **tools** (object) - Collection of all available tools from the server
- Each tool includes auto-inferred input schema

### Advantages
- Simpler implementation
- Automatically stays in sync with server changes
- No manual schema definition required

### Disadvantages
- No TypeScript type safety during development
- All server tools are loaded
- Limited IDE autocompletion

### Notes
- Best for exploratory development or when all server tools are needed
- Input types are inferred from server schemas
```

### GET /resources/{uri}

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/mcp-tools

Reads the contents of a specific resource by its URI. This endpoint retrieves the actual data from a resource identified by its unique URI.

```APIDOC
## GET /resources/{uri}

### Description
Reads and retrieves the contents of a specific resource identified by its URI.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/resources/{uri}

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **uri** (string) - Required - Unique resource identifier (e.g., file:///example/document.txt)

### Request Example
```typescript
const resourceData = await mcpClient.readResource({
  uri: 'file:///example/document.txt',
});
```

### Response
- **resourceData** (object) - Resource contents and metadata
  - Content format depends on resource type

### Notes
- URI format varies by resource type (file://, http://, etc.)
- Application controls when to fetch resources
- Resources provide context to the model
- Use listResources() first to discover available URIs
```

### Stream Text with Advanced Letta Configuration

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/letta

Advanced streaming example with comprehensive Letta provider options including agent configuration (maxSteps, includePings, streamTokens) and timeout settings. Suitable for complex reasoning chains and long-running operations.

```typescript
import { lettaCloud } from '@letta-ai/vercel-ai-sdk-provider';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: lettaCloud(),
  providerOptions: {
    letta: {
      agent: {
        id: 'your-agent-id',
        maxSteps: 100,
        includePings: true,
        streamTokens: true,
      },
      timeoutInSeconds: 300,
    },
  },
  prompt: 'Tell me a story about a robot learning to paint',
});
```

### Configure custom model settings with customProvider() in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/reference/ai-sdk-core/custom-provider

This example demonstrates how to use `customProvider` to define custom language models with specific settings, such as `reasoningEffort`. It shows how to replace a model with custom middleware and create an alias for another model, both using `openai` as the base provider. A fallback provider is also configured.

```ts
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { customProvider } from 'ai';

// custom provider with different model settings:
export const myOpenAI = customProvider({
  languageModels: {
    // replacement model with custom settings:
    'gpt-4': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
    // alias model with custom settings:
    'gpt-4o-reasoning-high': wrapLanguageModel({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      middleware: defaultSettingsMiddleware({
        settings: {
          providerOptions: {
            openai: {
              reasoningEffort: 'high',
            },
          },
        },
      }),
    }),
  },
  fallbackProvider: openai,
});
```

### Model Provider Configuration

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/nextjs-pages-router

Demonstrates how to configure different AI model providers with the AI SDK. Supports Vercel AI Gateway (default), OpenAI, and other first-party, OpenAI-compatible, and community providers.

```APIDOC
## Model Provider Configuration

### Description
Configure AI model providers for use with the streamText function. The AI SDK supports multiple provider options including Vercel AI Gateway, OpenAI, and community providers.

### Default Provider: Vercel AI Gateway

#### Method 1: String Reference (Recommended)
```typescript
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: 'anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5',
  messages: convertedMessages,
});
```

#### Method 2: Import from 'ai' Package
```typescript
import { gateway } from 'ai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
  messages: convertedMessages,
});
```

#### Method 3: Import from '@ai-sdk/gateway' Package
```typescript
import { gateway } from '@ai-sdk/gateway';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
  messages: convertedMessages,
});
```

### Using OpenAI Provider

#### Installation
```bash
pnpm add @ai-sdk/openai
# or
npm install @ai-sdk/openai
# or
yarn add @ai-sdk/openai
# or
bun add @ai-sdk/openai
```

#### Configuration
```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { streamText } from 'ai';

const result = streamText({
  model: openai('gpt-5.1'),
  messages: convertedMessages,
});
```

### Supported Providers
- **First-party**: Official AI SDK providers
- **OpenAI-compatible**: Providers with OpenAI-compatible APIs
- **Community**: Community-maintained provider packages

### Global Provider Configuration
Set a default global provider to use string model references throughout your application. This eliminates the need to specify the provider instance in every streamText call.

### Parameters
- **model** (string | LanguageModel) - Required - Model identifier or provider instance
- **messages** (ModelMessage[]) - Required - Converted message array without UI metadata

### Additional Settings
Pass additional configuration options to customize model behavior:
```typescript
const result = streamText({
  model: gateway('anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5'),
  messages: convertedMessages,
  temperature: 0.7,
  maxTokens: 1000,
  // ... other settings
});
```
```

        <div key={index} className="text-gray-500">
          <hr className="my-2 border-gray-300" />

    case 'text':
    // ...
    case 'tool-askForConfirmation':
    case 'tool-getLocation':
    case 'tool-getWeatherInformation':
    // ...
  }
});
// ...
```

### Process Tool Calls and Results with Claude Sonnet 4.5 in JavaScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/prompts

This JavaScript example demonstrates how to interact with an LLM (Claude Sonnet 4.5) using tool messages. It shows sending a multi-modal user message (text and image), receiving an assistant's 'tool-call' for nutrition data, and then responding with a 'tool-result' containing the requested JSON output. This pattern allows LLMs to trigger external functions and receive their outcomes.

```javascript
const result = await generateText({
  model: "anthropic/claude-sonnet-4.5",
  messages: [
    {
      role: 'user',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'text',
          text: 'How many calories are in this block of cheese?',
        },
        { type: 'image', image: fs.readFileSync('./data/roquefort.jpg') },
      ],
    },
    {
      role: 'assistant',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'tool-call',
          toolCallId: '12345',
          toolName: 'get-nutrition-data',
          input: { cheese: 'Roquefort' },
        },
        // there could be more tool calls here (parallel calling)
      ],
    },
    {
      role: 'tool',
      content: [
        {
          type: 'tool-result',
          toolCallId: '12345', // needs to match the tool call id
          toolName: 'get-nutrition-data',
          output: {
            type: 'json',
            value: {
              name: 'Cheese, roquefort',
              calories: 369,
              fat: 31,
              protein: 22,
            },
          },
        },
        // there could be more tool results here (parallel calling)
      ],
    },
  ],
});
```

### Constructing and Adding Tool Approval Responses in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/tools-and-tool-calling

This example illustrates how to create a `tool-approval-response` object based on an identified `tool-approval-request`. It shows how to set the `approved` status and an optional `reason`, then how to add these responses to the messages array for a subsequent model call.

```ts
import { type ToolApprovalResponse } from 'ai';

const approvals: ToolApprovalResponse[] = [];

for (const part of result.content) {
  if (part.type === 'tool-approval-request') {
    const response: ToolApprovalResponse = {
      type: 'tool-approval-response',
      approvalId: part.approvalId,
      approved: true, // or false to deny
      reason: 'User confirmed the command', // Optional context for the model
    };
    approvals.push(response);
  }
}

// add approvals to messages
messages.push({ role: 'tool', content: approvals });
```

### Configure MCP Tool with OpenAI Model

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/openai

Demonstrates how to set up an MCP (Model Context Protocol) server connection with OpenAI's gpt-5 model using the generateText function. The example shows connecting to a web-search MCP server with required serverLabel, serverUrl, and optional serverDescription parameters. This enables the model to call remote tools exposed by the MCP server.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: openai('gpt-5'),
  prompt: 'Search the web for the latest news about AI developments',
  tools: {
    mcp: openai.tools.mcp({
      serverLabel: 'web-search',
      serverUrl: 'https://mcp.exa.ai/mcp',
      serverDescription: 'A web-search API for AI agents',
    }),
  },
});
```

### Wrap Image Model with Middleware to Set Default Parameters

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/image-generation

Demonstrates how to use wrapImageModel and ImageModelV3Middleware to enhance image models by setting default values or implementing custom logic. This example sets a default size of 1024x1024 when none is provided in the request.

```typescript
import { generateImage, wrapImageModel } from 'ai';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

const model = wrapImageModel({
  model: openai.image('gpt-image-1'),
  middleware: {
    specificationVersion: 'v3',
    transformParams: async ({ params }) => ({
      ...params,
      size: params.size ?? '1024x1024',
    }),
  },
});

const { image } = await generateImage({
  model,
  prompt: 'Santa Claus driving a Cadillac',
});
```

### Create Streamable UI with streamUI function using AI SDK provider

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/migration-guides/migration-guide-3-1

Demonstrates the new streamUI function approach for creating streamable UIs with any compatible AI SDK provider. This example uses the AI SDK OpenAI provider and replaces the render key with generate for tool definitions, providing better provider flexibility.

```typescript
import { streamUI } from '@ai-sdk/rsc';
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { z } from 'zod';
import { Spinner, Weather } from '@/components';
import { getWeather } from '@/utils';

async function submitMessage(userInput = 'What is the weather in SF?') {
  'use server';

  const result = await streamUI({
    model: __MODEL__,
    system: 'You are a helpful assistant',
    messages: [{ role: 'user', content: userInput }],
    text: ({ content }) => <p>{content}</p>,
    tools: {
      get_city_weather: {
        description: 'Get the current weather for a city',
        parameters: z
          .object({
            city: z.string().describe('Name of the city'),
          })
          .required(),
        generate: async function* ({ city }) {
          yield <Spinner />;
          const weather = await getWeather(city);
          return <Weather info={weather} />;
        },
      },
    },
  });

  return result.value;
}
```

This event is only available when tool calls are streamed.

```TypeScript
{
  type: 'TextStreamPart',
  parameters: [
    {
      type: "'tool-call-streaming-start'",
      description:
        'Indicates the start of a tool call streaming. Only available when streaming tool calls.',
    },
    {
      name: 'toolCallId',
      type: 'string',
      description: 'The id of the tool call.',
    },
    {
      name: 'toolName',
      type: 'string',
      description:
        'The name of the tool, which typically would be the name of the function.',
    },
  ],
}
```

### Transform Messages Before Model Execution in ToolLoopAgent

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/loop-control

Demonstrates message modification in the prepareStep callback to optimize token usage. The example processes tool result messages and summarizes content exceeding 1000 characters before sending to the model, reducing token consumption while maintaining context.

```typescript
import { ToolLoopAgent } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;

const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  tools: {
    // your tools
  },
  prepareStep: async ({ messages, stepNumber }) => {
    // Summarize tool results to reduce token usage
    const processedMessages = messages.map(msg => {
      if (msg.role === 'tool' && msg.content.length > 1000) {
        return {
          ...msg,
          content: summarizeToolResult(msg.content),
        };
      }
      return msg;
    });

    return { messages: processedMessages };
  },
});

const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: '...',
});
```

### Display Anthropic Compaction Summary in AI SDK UI

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/anthropic

This React/JSX example shows how to identify and visually differentiate compaction summaries within a UI application using AI SDK's `useChat` or similar hooks. By inspecting the `providerMetadata` on message parts, developers can apply specific styling or UI elements to compaction summaries, improving user experience and clarity.

```tsx
{
  message.parts.map((part, index) => {
    if (part.type === 'text') {
      const isCompaction =
        (part.providerMetadata?.anthropic as { type?: string } | undefined)
          ?.type === 'compaction';

      if (isCompaction) {
        return (
          <div
            key={index}
            className="bg-yellow-100 border-l-4 border-yellow-500 p-2"
          >
            <span className="font-bold">[Compaction Summary]</span>
            <div>{part.text}</div>
          </div>
        );
      }
      return <div key={index}>{part.text}</div>;
    }
  });
}
```

### Generate Structured Text Output using FriendliAI Model with Regex

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/community-providers/friendliai

This example demonstrates how to constrain the output of a FriendliAI model using a regular expression. By passing a `regex` option to the model, you can ensure the generated text conforms to a specific pattern, which is highly useful for enforcing structured formats or restricting character sets.

```ts
import { friendli } from '@friendliai/ai-provider';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text } = await generateText({
  model: friendli('meta-llama-3.1-8b-instruct', {
    regex: new RegExp('[\n ,.?!0-9\uac00-\ud7af]*'),
  }),
  prompt: 'Who is the first king of the Joseon Dynasty?',
});

console.log(text);
```

### Define Agent-Wide and Per-Call Step Tracking

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/agents/building-agents

Configure onStepFinish at both constructor and method levels for comprehensive step tracking. Constructor callback executes first, followed by method-level callback for per-call tracking like billing.

```typescript
const agent = new ToolLoopAgent({
  model: __MODEL__,
  onStepFinish: async ({ usage }) => {
    // Agent-wide logging
    console.log('Agent step:', usage.totalTokens);
  },
});

// Method-level callback runs after constructor callback
const result = await agent.generate({
  prompt: 'Hello',
  onStepFinish: async ({ usage }) => {
    // Per-call tracking (e.g., for billing)
    await trackUsage(usage);
  },
});
```

### Configure User Tracking with Helicone (JavaScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/observability/helicone

This example illustrates how to add a `userId` to your AI requests using Helicone's `extraBody` option. Tracking users enables detailed analytics on individual user behavior, costs, and usage patterns within the Helicone dashboard.

```javascript
import { createHelicone } from '@helicone/ai-sdk-provider';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const helicone = createHelicone({
  apiKey: process.env.HELICONE_API_KEY,
});

const result = await generateText({
  model: helicone('gpt-4o-mini', {
    extraBody: {
      helicone: {
        userId: 'user@example.com',
      },

### Update Server Action to Explain SQL Queries with Zod Schema

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/cookbook/guides/natural-language-postgres

This updated TypeScript server action, `explainQuery`, now integrates the `explanationSchema` and specifies `output: 'array'` within the `generateObject` call. This enhancement ensures that the AI model returns an array of structured explanation objects, each strictly conforming to the defined schema. This provides a robust, type-safe, and predictable output for SQL query explanations.

```ts
// other imports
import { explanationSchema } from '@/lib/types';

/* ...rest of the file... */

export const explainQuery = async (input: string, sqlQuery: string) => {
  'use server';
  try {
    const result = await generateObject({
      model: 'openai/gpt-4o',
      system: `You are a SQL (postgres) expert. ...`, // SYSTEM PROMPT AS ABOVE - OMITTED FOR BREVITY
      prompt: `Explain the SQL query you generated to retrieve the data the user wanted. Assume the user is not an expert in SQL. Break down the query into steps. Be concise.

      User Query:
      ${input}

      Generated SQL Query:
      ${sqlQuery}`,
      schema: explanationSchema,
      output: 'array',
    });
    return result.object;
  } catch (e) {
    console.error(e);
    throw new Error('Failed to generate query');
  }
};
```

### Configure Parallel AI Search with Specific Parameters using generateText (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/ai-gateway

This example illustrates how to customize the `parallelSearch` tool by providing optional configuration parameters within `generateText`. It shows how to set the search `mode`, `maxResults`, `sourcePolicy` (including/excluding domains), and `excerpts` length for more refined web search queries.

```ts
import { gateway, generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  model: 'openai/gpt-5-nano',
  prompt: 'Find detailed information about TypeScript 5.0 features.',
  tools: {
    parallel_search: gateway.tools.parallelSearch({
      mode: 'agentic',
      maxResults: 5,
      sourcePolicy: {
        includeDomains: ['typescriptlang.org', 'github.com'],
      },
      excerpts: {
        maxCharsPerResult: 8000,
      },
    }),
  },
});

console.log(result.text);
console.log('Tool calls:', JSON.stringify(result.toolCalls, null, 2));
console.log('Tool results:', JSON.stringify(result.toolResults, null, 2));
```

### Add Weather Tool to AI Chatbot API Route (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/getting-started/expo

This TypeScript code updates the `app/api/chat+api.ts` file to include a `weather` tool. It leverages the `ai` SDK's `tool` function and `zod` for schema validation, enabling the chatbot to respond to weather-related queries by simulating data retrieval.

```tsx
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages, tool } from 'ai';
__PROVIDER_IMPORT__;
import { z } from 'zod';

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await req.json();

  const result = streamText({
    model: __MODEL__,
    messages: await convertToModelMessages(messages),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return {
            location,
            temperature,
          };
        },
      }),
    },
  });

  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse({
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/octet-stream',
      'Content-Encoding': 'none',
    },
  });
}
```

### Configure Anthropic Computer Tool in TypeScript

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/anthropic

This code illustrates the setup of the Anthropic Computer Tool, enabling AI models to control keyboard and mouse actions. It's initialized with `anthropic.tools.computer_20251124`, requiring display dimensions (`displayWidthPx`, `displayHeightPx`) and an `execute` method to implement actions like 'screenshot', 'zoom', 'type', or 'mouse_move'. The `toModelOutput` function maps the tool's results into a format consumable by the LLM, supporting both text and image outputs.

```ts
const computerTool = anthropic.tools.computer_20251124({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0, // Optional, for X11 environments
  enableZoom: true, // Optional, enables the zoom action

  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text, region }) => {
    // Implement your computer control logic here
    // Return the result of the action

    // Example code:
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        // multipart result:
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs
            .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
            .toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      case 'zoom': {
        // region is [x1, y1, x2, y2] defining the area to zoom into
        return {
          type: 'image',
          data: fs.readFileSync('./data/zoomed-region.png').toString('base64'),
        };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },

  // map to tool result content for LLM consumption:
  toModelOutput({ output }) {
    return typeof output === 'string'
      ? [{ type: 'text', text: output }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: output.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Combine URL Context and Google Search Tools with AI SDK (TypeScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-generative-ai

This example demonstrates how to simultaneously use both the `url_context` tool and the `google_search` tool within a single `generateText` call. This allows the model to leverage specific URL content for context while also performing a general web search for the latest information, providing a comprehensive grounding for its response.

```ts
import { google } from '@ai-sdk/google';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources, providerMetadata } = await generateText({
  model: google('gemini-2.5-flash'),
  prompt: `Based on this context: https://ai-sdk.dev/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-generative-ai, tell me how to use Gemini with AI SDK.
    Also, provide the latest news about AI SDK V5.`,
  tools: {
    google_search: google.tools.googleSearch({}),
    url_context: google.tools.urlContext({}),
  },
});

const metadata = providerMetadata?.google as
  | GoogleGenerativeAIProviderMetadata
  | undefined;
const groundingMetadata = metadata?.groundingMetadata;
const urlContextMetadata = metadata?.urlContextMetadata;
```
